The Three Ranks of Relative Species and the Solitary Species
Author defines four species types and discusses disagreements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four types of species (high, low, intermediate, solitary) and identify the key disagreements surrounding the solitary species.

Core Idea
Species classification reveals how logical definitions depend on hierarchical relations.

In logic, a species (naw') can be viewed in relation to higher and lower species. This passage from al-Bajuri's commentary on al-Bannani clarifies the three ranks of relative species and introduces the solitary species, which has no species above or below. The passage also exposes debates over the intellect and the point, illustrating how definitional disputes affect logical classification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three ranks of relative species
Find in the Arabic the three types: high, low, intermediate. Note the examples: body (jism) for high, human (insan) for low, animal (hayawan) for intermediate. Understand the relational definition: each is defined by what is above and below it.
2
Understand the solitary species
Locate the fourth type: the solitary species (al-naw' al-munfarid). It has no species above or below. The example given is the intellect ('aql). Note that there is disagreement about its classification.
Some later texts treat this as separate from relative species.
3
Examine the dispute over the intellect
The passage mentions two opinions: one treats 'aql as a solitary species (under the genus of separate substance), the other as a solitary genus (with unknown differentiate). Identify the difference: in the first, it has a genus; in the second, it has no genus.
4
Analyze the discussion on the point (nuqta)
See how the philosophers and theologians disagree on the nature of the point. This shows how definitions can change across disciplines. Relate this to the earlier classification: the point is debated similarly to 'aql.
5
Apply the classification to Islamic sciences
Consider how defining 'aql as a solitary species or genus impacts theological discussions about intellect and its relation to the soul and knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ مَرَاتِبَ النَّوْعِ الإِضَافِيِّ ثَلَاثَةٌ : (۱) - النَّوْعُ العَالِي، وَهُوَ : مَا لَا أَنْوَاعَ فَوْقَهُ، وَتَحْتَهُ الْأَنْوَاعُ : الجِسْمِ. (٢) - وَالنَّوْعُ السَّافِلُ، وَهُوَ : مَا لَا نَوْعَ تَحْتَهُ، وَفَوْقَهُ الْأَنْوَاعُ كَـ: «الإِنْسَانِ». (۳) - وَالنَّوْعُ المُتَوَسِّطُ، وَهُوَ : مَا فَوْقَهُ نَوْعٌ، وَتَحْتَهُ نَوْعٌ كَ: «الحَيَوَانِ». (٤) - وَبَقِيَ رَابِعٌ، وَهُوَ : النَّوْعُ المُنْفَرِدُ، وَهُوَ مَا لَا نَوْعَ فَوْقَهُ، وَلَا نَوْعَ تَحْتَهُ، وَيُمَثَلُ لَهُ بِالعَقْلِ ؛ بِنَاءٌ عَلَى نَوْعِيَّتِهِ . وَبُحِثَ فِيهِ : بِأَنَّا لَا نُسَلِّمُ عَدَمَ تَرَكُّبِ مَاهِيَّةِ البَسِيطِ مِنْ أَجْزَاءٍ ذِهْنِيَّةٍ كَمَا ذَكَرَهُ السَّعْدُ فِي شَرْحِ الشَّمْسِيَّةِ. ثُمَّ إِنَّهُ اخْتُلِفَ فِي «النُّقْطَةِ»: فَقِيلَ : مِنَ العَدَمِيَّاتِ . وَقِيلَ : مِنَ الاِعْتِبَارِيَّاتِ . وَقِيلَ : مِنَ الكَمِّيَّاتِ؛ هَذَا عِنْدَ الحُكَمَاءِ، وَأَمَّا عِنْدَ المُتَكَلِّمِينَ فَالنُّقْطَةُ الجَوْهَرُ الفَرْدُ. قَوْلُهُ : (بِنَاءً عَلَى نَوْعِيَّتِهِ) أَيْ كَوْنِهِ نَوْعاً، وَأَنَّ مَا تَحْتَهُ مِنَ العُقُولِ العَشَرَةِ أَفْرَادٌ اخْتَلَفَتْ بِالخَوَاصِّ. وَحَاصِلُ أَنَّ فِيهِ قَوْلَيْنِ: قَوْلٌ بِأَنَّهُ نَوْعٌ مُنْفَرِدٌ؛ أَيْ لَا نَوْعَ فَوْقَهُ وَلَا نَوْعَ تَحْتَهُ، بَلْ فَوْقَهُ جِنْسٌ وَهُوَ الجَوْهَرُ المُجَرَّدُ، وَتَحْتَهُ أَشْخَاصٌ. وَقَوْلٌ بِأَنَّهُ جِنْسٌ مُنْفَرِدٌ؛ أَيْ لَا فَوْقَهُ جِنْسٌ وَلَا تَحْتَهُ جِنْسٌ، بَلْ تَحْتَهُ أَنْوَاعٌ مُرَكَّبَةٌ مِنْهُ وَمِنْ فُصُولٍ تُمَيِّزُهَا، وَتِلْكَ الفُصُولُ لَا تُعْلَمُ، وَالجَوْهَرُ لَيْسَ جِنْساً لَهُ، بَلْ هُوَ عَرَضٌ عَامٌ لَهُ.
And know that the ranks of the relative species are three: (1) The high species, which is that which has no species above it, and below it are species, like 'body'. (2) The low species, which is that which has no species below it, and above it are species, like 'human'. (3) The intermediate species, which is that which has a species above it and a species below it, like 'animal'. (4) And there remains a fourth, which is the solitary species, and it is that which has no species above it and no species below it, and it is exemplified by the intellect, based on its being a species. And it was discussed in it: that we do not concede that the quiddity of the simple is not composed of mental parts, as al-Sa'd mentioned in his commentary on al-Shamsiyya. Then, there is disagreement about the point: some say it is among negations; some say it is among mental considerations; some say it is among quantities; this is according to the philosophers. As for the theologians, the point is the indivisible substance. His statement: 'based on its being a species' means its being a species, and that what is under it of the ten intellects are individuals differing by properties. The outcome is that there are two opinions: an opinion that it is a solitary species, i.e., no species above it and no species below it, but above it is a genus which is the separate substance, and below it are individuals. And an opinion that it is a solitary genus, i.e., no genus above it and no genus below it, but below it are species composed of it and of differentiating differentiate which are unknown, and substance is not a genus for it, but rather it is a universal accident for it.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of types of species (naw') from the perspective of relative species (al-naw' al-idafi). The author first enumerates three ranks: the high species (al-'ali) which has species under it but none above, exemplified by 'body' (jism); the low species (al-safil) which has species above but none below, exemplified by 'human' (insan); and the intermediate species (al-mutawassit) which has both a species above and below, exemplified by 'animal' (hayawan). Then a fourth type is added: the solitary species (al-munfarid), which has no species above or below, and is exemplified by the intellect ('aql) according to one opinion. The passage then discusses a critique: it is objected that the simplicity of quiddity is not accepted, as al-Sa'd al-Taftazani noted. Then there is a discussion about the point (nuqta): philosophers differ on whether it is a negation, mental consideration, or quantity; theologians consider it the indivisible substance (al-jawhar al-fard). The commentary then explains the phrase 'based on its being a species' regarding 'aql, clarifying that the ten intellects under it are individuals differing by properties. Finally, two opinions about 'aql are summarized: one group says it is a solitary species (under the genus of separate substance, with individuals under it); another says it is a solitary genus (with species under it composed of unknown differentiate, and substance is a universal accident, not a genus). This passage is a critical refinement (hanshiya) because it narrows down the disagreement.

Key Terms
النَّوْعُ الإِضَافِيُّ
النَّوْعُ المُنْفَرِدُ
العَقلُ
النُّقْطَةُ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of a low relative species?
A) Body (jism)
B) Human (insan)
C) Animal (hayawan)
D) Intellect ('aql)

Key Takeaway
The classification of species into relative and solitary highlights the relational nature of logical definitions and the importance of understanding hierarchies in conceptual analysis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given the classification, determine whether 'aql is a solitary species or solitary genus according to the two opinions. Identify the genus and differentiate for each opinion.
?
Consider the point (nuqta) as discussed by philosophers and theologians. Which categorization (negation, mental consideration, quantity, or indivisible substance) would make it a solitary species or not? Justify your answer.

The Three Types of Genus in Hierarchical Classification
Defines three types of genus with examples and clarifies the commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given genus as close, distant, intermediate, or isolated by applying the hierarchical criteria from the passage.

Core Idea
The three genera form a ladder from species to highest genus; isolated genus is a rare outlier.

In Islamic logic, the concept of genus is not monolithic. A genus can be close, distant, or intermediate depending on its position relative to other genera. This lesson unpacks each type using examples from the commentary, clarifying how they function in definitions and why the isolated genus is excluded. Understanding this classification sharpens your ability to analyze definitions in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Understand the hierarchical criterion
The three types are distinguished by whether a genus has a higher genus above it, a lower genus below it, both, or neither. The commentary uses 'no genus above' for distant, 'no genus below' for close, 'both above and below' for intermediate, and 'neither' for isolated.
2
Identify the close genus (jins qarīb)
Also called 'lowest genus', it has no genus under it. It is the immediate genus of a species. Example: 'animal' for 'human'. In any definition, the close genus is the most specific genus that directly subsumes the species.
3
Identify the distant genus (jins baʿīd)
Also called 'highest genus', it has no genus above it. In absolute terms, it is like 'substance'. However, the term 'distant' can be restricted: e.g., 'body' is distant by one rank from human, 'substance' by two ranks. This relativity is important in nuanced definitions.
The passage clarifies that only essential parts (constituents of quiddity) qualify; common accidents like 'thing' do not count.
4
Identify the intermediate genus (jins wasaṭ)
This genus has both a higher and a lower genus. Example: 'body' has 'substance' above and 'animal' below. It sits in the middle of the hierarchy.
5
Recognize the isolated genus (jins munfarid)
A genus with no higher or lower genus. Some scholars give 'intellect' as an example. It is excluded from the threefold division due to rarity and lack of clear instances.
The passage mentions that if isolated genus were included, the number of genus types would be four.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في مباحث الألفاظ (۳۲) وَأَوَّلُ ثَلَاثَةٌ بِلَا شَطَط: جنس قريب، أو بعيد، أو وسط وخرج بقولنا : في جواب : بقطع النظر عن الإضافة لـ «أي» : العرض العام؛ لما مر . ومع النظر لها : الجنس، والنوع؛ لما تقدم . وبقولنا : في عرضه» : الفصل؛ لأنه يصدق في جواب أي شيء هو في ذاته؟، كما علمت . قوله : (وأول) أي : الذي هو الجنس . وقوله : (ثلاثة) أي : بقطع النظر عن الجنس المنفرد؛ لعدم الظفر بمثاله، وإلا فمع النظر إليه يكون الجنس أربعة، ومثل بعضهم للجنس المنفرد بـ : «العقل»؛ بناء على جنسيته . وقوله : ( بلا شطط) أي : بلا زيادة؛ يعني: ولا نقص، ففي كلامه اكتفاء . قال بعضهم : أصل قوله : بلا شطط» : لا بشطط (۱)؛ لأن حق حرف النفي التقديم على جميع المنفي (۲) ، وهو الباء) مع الشطط الدال مجموعهما على ملابسة الثلاثة للشطط (۱) ، وإنما قدمت الباء تزييناً للفظ . وهذا إنما يتجه (۲) على القول بأن لا في مثل ذلك ليست بمعنى : «غير»، وأما على القول بأنها بمعنى : غير كما هو المشهور في نحو قولك : (جنت بلا زاد فلا، فليعرف . قوله : (جنس قريب) ويسمى : الجنس السافل»، وهو ما لا جنس تحته، وفوقه الأجناس ؛ كـ: «الحيوان». وقوله : أو بعيد) «أو هنا وفيما بعد بمعنى: «الواو) . ويسمى البعيد : الجنس العالي وهو ما لا جنس فوقه، وتحته الأجناس؛ كـ : «الجوهر»، وهذا عند الإطلاق، وأما عند التفييد ؛ كان يقال : بعيد بمرتبة ، أو بمرتبتين، فهو بحسب القيد الذي قيد به، فالأول كـ : الجسم»، والثاني كـ: (الجوهر (۳) وقوله : أو وسط هو : ما فوقه جنس ، وتحته جنس؛ كـ: «الجسم). الأنبابي : قوله : (تزينا للفظ) أي: تحسيناً له. أقول : قد يتوقف في وجه التزيين، وما يتوهم من أن وجهه : خفة اللفظ وعذوبته بهذا التقديم، يرد : بأن ذلك على تسليمه إنما نشأ من كثرة استعمال اللفظ هكذا، وألفته على هذا الوجه، فلو استعمل وألف بدون التقديم لحصلت تلك العذوبة والخفّة، فافهم . اهـ «صبان (٤) . قوله : (كـ: الجوهر) لا يقال : هناك ما هو أعلى منه كالشيء والمذكور والموجود والحادث. لأنّا نقول : هذه أعراض عامة خارجة عن الماهيات؛ أي: لم يجعل شيء منها جزء ماهية أصلاً، فلا يكون من الجنس الذي الكلام فيه؛ لأنه لا بد أن يكون جزءاً من حقيقة، أفاده الملوي في «كبيره»(٥) . اهـ «صبان (٦).

His statement: (or distant) 'or' here and in what follows is in the meaning of 'and'. And the distant is called the highest genus, and it is that which has no genus above it, and under it there are genera; like 'substance', and this is in absolute terms, but when restricted, as if it is said: distant by one rank or by two ranks, then it is according to the restriction by which it is restricted, so the first is like 'body', and the second like 'substance'. His statement: (or intermediate) it is that which has a genus above it and a genus under it; like 'body'. Al-Anbabi: His statement: (as embellishment for the wording) meaning as beautification for it. I say: one may hesitate regarding the aspect of embellishment, and what is supposed that its aspect is ease and sweetness of the wording with this fronting, is refuted: because that, if granted, only arose from the frequent usage of the wording in this way and its familiarity in this manner, so if it were used and familiar without the fronting, that ease and sweetness would be obtained, so understand. End quote from al-Sabban. His statement: (like substance) it cannot be said: there is what is higher than it like 'thing', 'mentioned', 'existent', and 'occurring'. Because we say: these are common accidents external to the quiddities; meaning none of them is made a part of a quiddity at all, so they are not from the genus under discussion, because it is necessary that it be a part of a reality, as al-Malawi stated in his 'Kabir'. End quote from al-Sabban.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage, from the commentary on the matn, defines the three types of genus that serve as the first answer to the question 'what is it?' (ما هو). The author begins by stating that the first genera are three: close, distant, and intermediate. He then clarifies that 'close genus' (also called 'lowest genus') is one that has no genus beneath it—like 'animal' in relation to humans; it is the immediate genus. The 'distant genus' (or 'highest genus') has no genus above it—like 'substance', which is the highest category. The 'intermediate genus' has a genus both above and below—like 'body', which is under substance and above animal. The passage then delves into grammatical analysis of 'بلا شطط' (without excess), explaining that it means without increase or deficiency, and discusses the placement of the negation particle. It also mentions the concept of an 'isolated genus' (جنس منفرد), like 'intellect' according to some, which does not fit the threefold division due to lack of examples. The commentary further refines the definitions by noting that 'distant' can be relative to restrictions (e.g., two ranks away), and it underscores that only essential parts (essential genera) are considered, excluding common accidents like 'thing' or 'existent' which are not parts of the quiddity. This passage is an expansion of the matn, providing examples and resolving potential ambiguities.

Key Terms
جنس قريب
جنس بعيد
جنس وسط
جنس منفرد
بلا شطط

Key Takeaway
The type of genus is determined by its position in the hierarchy: close has no subgenus, distant has no supergenus, intermediate has both, and isolated stands alone.

The Five Relationships of Words to Meanings
Enumeration of five word-meaning relationships and their classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the five relationships between words and meanings into the three categories based on the relata involved.

Core Idea
Words relate to meanings in five ways, divided by whether the relation is between a meaning and its instances, between two meanings, or between a word and its meaning.

In this passage, al-Bajuri enumerates the five classical relationships between expressions (alfāẓ) and meanings (maʿānī). He then groups them into three types based on what the relationship actually connects: a meaning to its individuals, one meaning to another meaning, or a word to its meaning. This classification is essential for understanding how definitions and arguments work in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of relationships
Al-Bajuri first groups the five relationships by what they connect: (1) meaning to its individuals, (2) meaning of one word to meaning of another word, (3) word to its meaning, and (4) word to another word. Note that (3) and (4) are actually two sides of the same coin? Actually (3) is word to its meaning, (4) is word to another word, but both involve the word directly.
Be precise about the category boundaries.
2
Name the specific relationships in each category
For each category, list the relationships: (1) tawāṭu' and tashkīk; (2) tabāyun; (3) ishtirāk; (4) tarāduf. Understand why tarāduf is a separate category between two words.
Tarāduf is between two words with the same meaning, not directly between word and its meaning.
3
Provide concrete examples from Arabic
Find an example for each: tawāṭu': 'insān' (human) applies equally to Zayd and Amr. Tashkīk: 'wujūd' (existence) applies primarily to God and secondarily to creation. Tabāyun: 'insān' and 'faras' (horse). Ishtirāk: 'ʿayn' (eye, spring, spy). Tarāduf: 'laysa' and 'mā' for negation.
Ensure examples are from Islamic sciences, e.g., fiqh terms.
4
Distinguish tawāṭu' from ishtirāk
Tawāṭu' has one meaning applied to multiple instances; ishtirāk has multiple meanings for one word. They are opposite: one meaning vs multiple meanings.
Students often confuse them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ فِي بَيَانِ نِسْبَةِ الْأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي (٣٣) وَنِسْبَةُ الْأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي خَمْسَةُ أَقْسَامٍ بِلَا نُقْصَانِ. الْبَاجُورِيُّ: قَوْلُهُ: (فَصْلٌ فِي بَيَانِ نِسْبَةِ الْأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي) اعْلَمْ أَنَّ مَا ذَكَرَهُ الْمُصَنِّفُ مِنَ النِّسَبِ الْخَمْسَةِ: (١) مِنْهُ مَا هُوَ مُعْتَبَرٌ بَيْنَ مَعْنَى اللَّفْظِ وَأَفْرَادِهِ، وَذَلِكَ هُوَ: التَّوَاطُؤُ، وَالتَّشْكِيكُ. (٣) وَمِنْهُ مَا هُوَ مُعْتَبَرٌ بَيْنَ اللَّفْظِ وَمَعْنَاهُ، وَذَلِكَ هُوَ: الِاشْتِرَاكُ. (٤) وَمِنْهُ مَا هُوَ مُعْتَبَرٌ بَيْنَ لَفْظٍ وَلَفْظٍ آخَرَ، وَذَلِكَ هُوَ: التَّرَادُفُ. وَظَاهِرُ قَوْلِ الْمُصَنِّفِ: وَنِسْبَةُ الْأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي لَا يَفِي إِلَّا بِالَّذِي بَيْنَ اللَّفْظِ وَمَعْنَاهُ وَهُوَ الِاشْتِرَاكُ، وَإِذَا كَانَ كَذَلِكَ فَكَيْفَ يُخْبِرُ عَنْهُ بِقَوْلِهِ: خَمْسَةُ أَقْسَامٍ؟ وَأَجَابَ بَعْضُهُمْ: بِأَنَّ فِي كَلَامِ الْمُصَنِّفِ اكْتِفَاءً؛ وَالتَّقْدِيرُ: وَنِسْبَةُ الْأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي وَلِلْأَلْفَاظِ، وَنِسْبَةُ الْمَعَانِي لِلْمَعَانِي وَلِلْأَفْرَادِ. وَجَعَلَ الشَّيْخُ الْمَلَّوِيُّ اللَّامَ فِي قَوْلِهِ: لِلْمَعَانِي بِمَعْنَى مَعَ، وَجَعَلَ الْمُرَادَ مِنَ الْمَعَانِي مَا يَشْمَلُ الْأَفْرَادَ، وَعَلَيْهِ فَيَصِيرُ كَلَامُ الْمُصَنِّفِ هَكَذَا: وَنِسْبَةُ الْأَلْفَاظِ مَعَ نِسْبَةِ الْمَعَانِي، وَلَا شَكَّ أَنَّ هَذَا يَصْدُقُ بِنِسْبَةِ الْأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي وَلِلْأَلْفَاظِ وَنِسْبَةِ الْمَعَانِي لِلْمَعَانِي إِمَّا حَقِيقَةً أَوْ بِمَعْنَى الْأَفْرَادِ، فَلْيُتَأَمَّلْ.
Section on explaining the relationship of expressions to meanings. (33) And the relationship of expressions to meanings is five divisions without deficiency. Al-Bajuri: His statement: 'Section on explaining the relationship of expressions to meanings' — know that what the author mentioned of the five relationships: (1) Among them is what is considered between the meaning of the expression and its individuals, and that is: univocality (tawāṭu') and gradation (tashkīk). (2) And among them is what is considered between the meaning of an expression and the meaning of another expression, and that is: contrast (tabāyun), and whatever judgment of contrast occurs between expressions, it is with regard to their meanings. (3) And among them is what is considered between the expression and its meaning, and that is: homonymy (ishtirāk). (4) And among them is what is considered between an expression and another expression, and that is: synonymy (tarāduf). And the apparent meaning of the author's statement: 'And the relationship of expressions to meanings' only suffices for what is between the expression and its meaning, namely homonymy. If that is the case, how does he inform about it with his statement: 'five divisions'? And some answered: that in the author's speech there is brevity; and the estimation is: the relationship of expressions to meanings and to expressions, and the relationship of meanings to meanings and to individuals. And Shaykh al-Mallawi made the lām in his statement 'to meanings' in the sense of 'with', and made the intended meaning of 'meanings' to include individuals, and accordingly the author's statement becomes like this: 'and the relationship of expressions with the relationship of meanings', and there is no doubt that this is true for the relationship of expressions to meanings and to expressions and the relationship of meanings to meanings, either literally or in the sense of individuals, so let it be considered.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on the relationship between words (alfāẓ) and their meanings (maʿānī). The matn states that there are five types of such relationships, without any deficiency. Al-Bajuri then expands on this by explaining the five types in detail. First, there is the relationship that exists between the meaning of a word and its individual instances (afrād). This type covers two sub-relationships: tawāṭu' (univocality), where the meaning applies equally to all individuals (e.g., 'human' applies equally to Zayd and ʿAmr), and tashkīk (gradation/equivocality by analogy), where the meaning applies to individuals in different degrees (e.g., 'existence' applies to God and creation in a graded manner). Second, there is the relationship between the meaning of one word and the meaning of another word. This is tabāyun (contrast), where meanings are completely different (e.g., 'human' and 'horse'). Any judgment of contrast between words is based on their meanings. Third, there is the relationship between a single word and its meaning, which is ishtirāk (homonymy), where one word has multiple unrelated meanings (e.g., 'ʿayn' can mean eye, spring, spy). Fourth, there is the relationship between one word and another word, which is tarāduf (synonymy), where two different words share the same meaning (e.g., 'laysa' and 'mā' in Arabic for negation). After enumerating these, al-Bajuri addresses a potential objection: the author's phrasing 'relationship of expressions to meanings' seems only to cover homonymy (type 3), not all five. Two solutions are offered: (1) Some say the author omitted some words, meaning the relationship of expressions to meanings and to expressions, and meanings to meanings and to individuals. (2) Al-Mallawī interpreted the lām in 'to meanings' as meaning 'with', so it reads 'the relationship of expressions with the relationship of meanings', implying a broader scope. The commentator leaves this for the reader to ponder.

Key Terms
التواطؤ
التشكيك
التباين
الاشتراك
الترادف

Key Takeaway
The five relationships are divided into three categories based on what the relation connects: meaning to its instances, meaning to another meaning, word to its meaning, or word to another word.

Resolving the Apparent Contradiction in the Phrasing
Resolution of a textual ambiguity in enumerating the five relationships.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the two interpretive solutions proposed by al-Bajuri to reconcile the author's wording with the five relationships enumerated.

Core Idea
The phrase 'relationship of expressions to meanings' literally covers only ishtirāk, but scholars resolve it through ellipsis or a broader interpretation of 'meanings'.

After listing the five relationships, al-Bajuri raises an apparent problem: the title says 'relationship of expressions to meanings,' which only seems to cover ishtirāk (the relation between a word and its meaning). He then presents two solutions: one suggests ellipsis, the other reinterprets 'meanings' to include individuals and other meanings. This lesson examines how commentators handle textual precision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent contradiction
The phrase 'relationship of expressions to meanings' naturally suggests only the relation between a word and its meaning (ishtirāk). But the author claims there are five relationships. So either the phrase is incomplete or it is interpreted more broadly.
Understand why the phrase seems insufficient.
2
Explain the first solution: ellipsis
Some scholars say the author omitted words, implying a fuller meaning: 'relationship of expressions to meanings and to expressions, and the relationship of meanings to meanings and to individuals.'
This is a common tawjīh technique called takmīl (completion).
3
Explain the second solution: reinterpretation
Al-Mallawi reinterprets the lām (to) as maʿa (with), and takes 'meanings' to include individuals. So the phrase becomes 'relationship of expressions with the relationship of meanings,' which can cover all five.
This shifts the scope of 'meanings' to encompass individuals and other meanings.

فَصْلٌ فِي بَيَانِ نِسْبَةِ الْأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي (٣٣) وَنِسْبَةُ الْأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي خَمْسَةُ أَقْسَامٍ بِلَا نُقْصَانِ. الْبَاجُورِيُّ: قَوْلُهُ: (فَصْلٌ فِي بَيَانِ نِسْبَةِ الْأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي) اعْلَمْ أَنَّ مَا ذَكَرَهُ الْمُصَنِّفُ مِنَ النِّسَبِ الْخَمْسَةِ: (١) مِنْهُ مَا هُوَ مُعْتَبَرٌ بَيْنَ مَعْنَى اللَّفْظِ وَأَفْرَادِهِ، وَذَلِكَ هُوَ: التَّوَاطُؤُ، وَالتَّشْكِيكُ. (٢) وَمِنْهُ مَا هُوَ مُعْتَبَرٌ بَيْنَ مَعْنَى لَفْظٍ وَمَعْنَى لَفْظٍ آخَرَ، وَذَلِكَ هُوَ: التَّبَايُنُ، وَمَا قَدْ يَقَعُ مِنَ الْحُكْمِ بِالتَّبَايُنِ بَيْنَ الْأَلْفَاظِ فَهُوَ بِالنَّظَرِ لِمَعَانِيهَا. (٣) وَمِنْهُ مَا هُوَ مُعْتَبَرٌ بَيْنَ اللَّفْظِ وَمَعْنَاهُ، وَذَلِكَ هُوَ: الِاشْتِرَاكُ. (٤) وَمِنْهُ مَا هُوَ مُعْتَبَرٌ بَيْنَ لَفْظٍ وَلَفْظٍ آخَرَ، وَذَلِكَ هُوَ: التَّرَادُفُ. وَظَاهِرُ قَوْلِ الْمُصَنِّفِ: وَنِسْبَةُ الْأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي لَا يَفِي إِلَّا بِالَّذِي بَيْنَ اللَّفْظِ وَمَعْنَاهُ وَهُوَ الِاشْتِرَاكُ، وَإِذَا كَانَ كَذَلِكَ فَكَيْفَ يُخْبِرُ عَنْهُ بِقَوْلِهِ: خَمْسَةُ أَقْسَامٍ؟ وَأَجَابَ بَعْضُهُمْ: بِأَنَّ فِي كَلَامِ الْمُصَنِّفِ اكْتِفَاءً؛ وَالتَّقْدِيرُ: وَنِسْبَةُ الْأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي وَلِلْأَلْفَاظِ، وَنِسْبَةُ الْمَعَانِي لِلْمَعَانِي وَلِلْأَفْرَادِ. وَجَعَلَ الشَّيْخُ الْمَلَّوِيُّ اللَّامَ فِي قَوْلِهِ: لِلْمَعَانِي بِمَعْنَى مَعَ، وَجَعَلَ الْمُرَادَ مِنَ الْمَعَانِي مَا يَشْمَلُ الْأَفْرَادَ، وَعَلَيْهِ فَيَصِيرُ كَلَامُ الْمُصَنِّفِ هَكَذَا: وَنِسْبَةُ الْأَلْفَاظِ مَعَ نِسْبَةِ الْمَعَانِي، وَلَا شَكَّ أَنَّ هَذَا يَصْدُقُ بِنِسْبَةِ الْأَلْفَاظِ لِلْمَعَانِي وَلِلْأَلْفَاظِ وَنِسْبَةِ الْمَعَانِي لِلْمَعَانِي إِمَّا حَقِيقَةً أَوْ بِمَعْنَى الْأَفْرَادِ، فَلْيُتَأَمَّلْ.
Section on explaining the relationship of expressions to meanings. (33) And the relationship of expressions to meanings is five divisions without deficiency. Al-Bajuri: His statement: 'Section on explaining the relationship of expressions to meanings' — know that what the author mentioned of the five relationships: (1) Among them is what is considered between the meaning of the expression and its individuals, and that is: univocality (tawāṭu') and gradation (tashkīk). (2) And among them is what is considered between the meaning of an expression and the meaning of another expression, and that is: contrast (tabāyun), and whatever judgment of contrast occurs between expressions, it is with regard to their meanings. (3) And among them is what is considered between the expression and its meaning, and that is: homonymy (ishtirāk). (4) And among them is what is considered between an expression and another expression, and that is: synonymy (tarāduf). And the apparent meaning of the author's statement: 'And the relationship of expressions to meanings' only suffices for what is between the expression and its meaning, namely homonymy. If that is the case, how does he inform about it with his statement: 'five divisions'? And some answered: that in the author's speech there is brevity; and the estimation is: the relationship of expressions to meanings and to expressions, and the relationship of meanings to meanings and to individuals. And Shaykh al-Mallawi made the lām in his statement 'to meanings' in the sense of 'with', and made the intended meaning of 'meanings' to include individuals, and accordingly the author's statement becomes like this: 'and the relationship of expressions with the relationship of meanings', and there is no doubt that this is true for the relationship of expressions to meanings and to expressions and the relationship of meanings to meanings, either literally or in the sense of individuals, so let it be considered.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on the relationship between words (alfāẓ) and their meanings (maʿānī). The matn states that there are five types of such relationships, without any deficiency. Al-Bajuri then expands on this by explaining the five types in detail. First, there is the relationship that exists between the meaning of a word and its individual instances (afrād). This type covers two sub-relationships: tawāṭu' (univocality), where the meaning applies equally to all individuals (e.g., 'human' applies equally to Zayd and ʿAmr), and tashkīk (gradation/equivocality by analogy), where the meaning applies to individuals in different degrees (e.g., 'existence' applies to God and creation in a graded manner). Second, there is the relationship between the meaning of one word and the meaning of another word. This is tabāyun (contrast), where meanings are completely different (e.g., 'human' and 'horse'). Any judgment of contrast between words is based on their meanings. Third, there is the relationship between a single word and its meaning, which is ishtirāk (homonymy), where one word has multiple unrelated meanings (e.g., 'ʿayn' can mean eye, spring, spy). Fourth, there is the relationship between one word and another word, which is tarāduf (synonymy), where two different words share the same meaning (e.g., 'laysa' and 'mā' in Arabic for negation). After enumerating these, al-Bajuri addresses a potential objection: the author's phrasing 'relationship of expressions to meanings' seems only to cover homonymy (type 3), not all five. Two solutions are offered: (1) Some say the author omitted some words, meaning the relationship of expressions to meanings and to expressions, and meanings to meanings and to individuals. (2) Al-Mallawī interpreted the lām in 'to meanings' as meaning 'with', so it reads 'the relationship of expressions with the relationship of meanings', implying a broader scope. The commentator leaves this for the reader to ponder.

بمعنى مع

Key Takeaway
The apparent contradiction between a text's wording and its content can be resolved by positing ellipsis or reinterpreting key terms, a common practice in Islamic hermeneutics.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Definer (Mu'arraf) and Its Two Types
Definition of the definer and its two types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the definer (mu'arraf) in a definition and distinguish between a complete definition (hadd tamm) and other types based on the two senses of conception.

Core Idea
The definer must be known; the defined must be unknown — or definition fails.

In this lesson, we examine the foundational concept of a 'definer' (mu'arraf) — the tool by which we come to know something. The passage clarifies that not everything called a definition is equal: some give complete knowledge, others only partial. The key lies in understanding the two roles of conception (tasawwur).

Guided Path
1
Identify the definer and the defined
The term 'mu'arraf' has two forms: with kasr ra (the definer) and with fatha ra (the defined). Locate these in the Arabic and note their different roles.
The diacritic (kasr vs fatha) is the only difference in writing.
2
Extract the definition of the definer
The definer is defined as 'that whose conception necessitates conception of the defined and its distinction from others.' Break this into two parts: (1) giving conception of the defined, (2) distinguishing it from others.
The first part (conception) is the complete definition; the second part covers all other definitions.
3
Understand the two senses of 'tasawwur'
The word 'tasawwur' is used in two different meanings in the definition. For the definer, it means 'mental occurrence' (khutur bi al-bal) — the definer must already be present in the mind. For the defined, it means 'acquisition from ignorance' (husul 'an jahl) — the defined must be unknown initially.
This dual usage avoids circularity: defining the unknown by the unknown, or defining what is already known.
4
Distinguish the two types of definitions
The 'first' (conception of the defined) refers to the complete definition (hadd tamm). The 'second' (distinction from others) includes all other definitions: incomplete definition (hadd naqis), description (rasm), and verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi).
The commentary clarifies that the complete definition gives full knowledge; the others give only distinction or partial conception.

فصل في المعرفات
(فصل في المعرفات)
قوله: (في المعرفات جمع: «معرف) - بكسر الراء، وهو: ما يقتضي تصوره تصور المعرف بفتح الراء -، وامتيازه عن غيره»؛ فالأول: الحد التام، والثاني: ما عداه مما سيأتي والمراد بالتصور الأول: الخطور بالبال، لا الحصول عن جهل؛ لأن المعرف - بكسر الراء - يجب أن يكون معلوماً حال التعريف به، وإلا لزم التعريف بالمجهول. وبالتصور الثاني: الحصول عن جهل، لا الخطور بالبال؛ لأن المعرف - بفتح الراء - يجب أن يكون مجهولاً حال تعريفه، وإلا لزم تحصيل الحاصل.
الأنبابي
قوله: (ما يقتضي تصوره تصور المعرف من جملة ما أورده البناني على قول السنوسي: «المعرف للحقيقة ما معرفته سبب لمعرفة تلك الحقيقة : أنه يقتضي أن مجرد تصور المعرف سبب في تصور الحقيقة، وليس : كذلك، بل السبب مجموع أمرين: التصور المذكور، وحمل المعرف على الحقيقة، ولهذا عرف في «التهذيب» المعرف بـ : ما يقال على الشيء لإفادة تصوره، ثم أورد سؤالاً وجواباً على ذلك، فراجعه. قوله: (والمراد بالتصور الأول... إلخ ) ولا يرد: أنه استعمل لفظ «التصور» في التعريف في المعنيين، هو في أحدهما حقيقة، وفي الآخر مجاز، أو مشترك فيهما؛ لعدم اللبس. اهـ «صبان
(۱) في المطبوع: «أو امتيازه» بدلاً من وامتيازه».
فراجعه
(۲) الشرشيمي: قوله: (ما عداه) أي: من الحد الناقص، والرسم مطلقاً، والتعريف اللفظي.
(۳) الشرشيمي: قوله: (الخطور بالبال) لا يخفى أن التصور بهذا المعنى مجاز، والحدود تصان عن المجاز. ويجاب: بأن هناك قرينة معينة للمراد، وهي أن المعرف - بكسر الراء - يجب أن يكون معلوماً قبل التعريف به؛ بحيث لو خطر بالبال محمولاً على المعرف ـ بفتح الراء ـ لفهم ذلك المعرف.
(٤) الشرشيمي: قوله: (لا الخطور بالبال إلى قوله: (وإلا لزم تحصيل الحاصل) أي: لو كان المراد من التصور الثاني الخطور، لكان المعرف معلوماً، فيلزم على تعريفه تحصيل الحاصل، وهو علم المعلوم، وهذا معنى كلامه، وفيه نظر؛ لأنه حيث كان المراد من التصور: الخطور، وهو لا يكون إلا عن غفلةٍ، ولا يلزم تحصيل الحاصل إلا بتحصيل إدراك جديد للمعلوم الذي لم يحصل فيه ذهول وغفلة، وإلا لزم تحصيل الحاصل من التعريف عند خطوره بالبال، فكان الأنسب أن يقول: (وإلا لم يحتج إلى تعريف؛ لأن الخطور لا يتوقف على ذلك، بل يحصل بمجرد الالتفات.
(٥) انظر: حاشية البناني على شرح مختصر السنوسي في المنطق، مخطوط الأزهرية برقم (١٥٩٧٠) (ق: ۲۸).
(٦) انظر: حاشية الصبان على الشرح الصغير للملوي، (ص: ۳۰۹).
Chapter on Definers. (Chapter on Definers) His statement: 'Definers (plural of 'mu'arraf' - with kasr of the ra') is that whose conception necessitates the conception of the defined (with fatha of the ra') and its distinction from others'; so the first is the complete definition, and the second is what other than it that will come. And what is meant by the first 'conception' is the occurrence in the mind, not the acquisition from ignorance; because the definer (with kasr of the ra') must be known at the time of definition by it, otherwise it would be definition by the unknown. And by the second 'conception' is the acquisition from ignorance, not the occurrence in the mind; because the defined (with fatha of the ra') must be unknown at the time of its definition, otherwise it would be attainment of what is already attained. al-Anbabi: His statement: ('What its conception necessitates conception of the defined...') is among what al-Bannani adduced against al-Sanusi's statement: 'The definer of the reality is that whose knowledge is the cause of knowledge of that reality' — that it implies that mere conception of the definer is the cause of conception of the reality, which is not so; rather the cause is a combination of two things: the mentioned conception and the predication of the definer on the reality. For this reason, in 'al-Tahdhib' the definer is defined as 'what is said of a thing to give conception of it', then he posed a question and answer on that, so refer to it. His statement: ('And what is meant by the first conception... etc.') And it is not objected that he used the word 'tasawwur' in the definition in two senses, it being used literally in one and figuratively in the other, or as a homonym; because there is no confusion. End. [from] al-Sabban. (1) In the printed version: 'or its distinction' instead of 'and its distinction'. Refer to it. (2) al-Sharshimi: His statement: ('what other than it') i.e., from the incomplete definition, and the description in absolute sense, and the verbal definition. (3) al-Sharshimi: His statement: ('occurrence in the mind') it is not hidden that 'tasawwur' in this sense is figurative, and definitions are kept free from figurative language. And it is responded: that there is a specific contextual clue for the intended meaning, which is that the definer (with kasr of the ra') must be known before definition by it, such that if it occurs in the mind predicated on the defined (with fatha of the ra'), that defined is understood. (4) al-Sharshimi: His statement: ('not the occurrence in the mind' until his saying: ('otherwise attainment of what is already attained would follow') i.e., if what was meant by the second 'tasawwur' were occurrence, then the defined would be known, and then its definition would entail attainment of what is already attained, which is knowledge of the known, and this is the meaning of his words, and there is consideration in it; because since what is meant by 'tasawwur' is occurrence, which only occurs from heedlessness, and attainment of what is already attained only results from attaining a new perception of the known in which there was no forgetfulness or heedlessness; otherwise attainment of what is already attained would follow from definition when it occurs in the mind. So it would be more appropriate to say: 'otherwise it would not need definition; because occurrence does not depend on that, but rather happens by mere attention.' (5) See: Hashiyat al-Bannani on Sharh Mukhtasar al-Sanusi in Logic, al-Azhar manuscript no. (15970) (folio: 28). (6) See: Hashiyat al-Sabban on al-Sharh al-Saghir lil-Mallawi, (p. 309).
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter heading 'Fasl fi al-mu'arrafat' (Chapter on Definers). The commentator, al-Bajuri, begins by explaining the term 'mu'arrafat' as the plural of 'mu'arraf' (with kasr ra), which is defined as something whose conception (tasawwur) necessitates the conception of the defined (mu'arraf with fatha ra) and also its distinction from other things. The first part (conception of the defined) constitutes the complete definition (hadd tamm), while the second part (distinction) covers other types of definition (incomplete definition, description, verbal definition). A crucial point is the dual meaning of 'tasawwur'. The first meaning (used for the definer) is 'khutur bi al-bal' (occurrence in the mind or mental presence), not 'husul 'an jahl' (acquisition from ignorance), because the definer must be known beforehand to avoid defining by the unknown. The second meaning (used for the defined) is 'husul 'an jahl' (acquisition from ignorance), not mere mental occurrence, because the defined must be unknown at the time of definition to avoid tautology (tahsil al-hasil). Marginal notes add further precision: al-Anbabi notes that al-Bannani criticized al-Sanusi's definition because mere conception of the definer is insufficient; one must also predicate it of the defined. al-Sharshimi discusses the figurative use of 'tasawwur' for mental occurrence, justifying it by the presence of contextual clues. He also critiques the phrasing about tahsil al-hasil, arguing that if the defined is merely forgotten, definition does not entail impossibility but rather re-acquisition.

Key Takeaway
The definer must be mentally present (khutur) and the defined initially unknown (jahl) to avoid circularity or tautology in definition.

Defining the Definiens and the Two Senses of Tasawwur
Bajuri defines the term معرف and distinguishes two meanings of تصور in the definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two meanings of tasawwur in the definition of mu'arraf and explain why each meaning is necessary for a valid definition.

Core Idea
A definition uses a known definiens to reveal an unknown definiendum—requiring two distinct senses of 'conception'.

In this passage, Bajuri sharpens a crucial distinction within the definition of 'definiens'. He shows that the term 'tasawwur' (conception) carries two different meanings in one sentence: the first as mere mental presence, the second as knowledge after ignorance. Understanding this precision prevents the logical errors of defining by an unknown or repeating the known. We will walk through his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Locate the term 'مُعَرِّف' (with kasr of ra). Bajuri states it is the definiens: that which, when conceived, yields conception of the definiendum and distinguishes it.
2
Extract the two occurrences of 'tasawwur'
In the phrase 'تَصَوُّرُهُ تَصَوُّرَ المَعرَّفِ', the first 'tasawwur' refers to the conception of the definiens, and the second to the conception of the definiendum. Bajuri then assigns a specific meaning to each.
3
Understand why the first 'tasawwur' means mere mental occurrence
Bajuri argues that the definiens must already be known; otherwise, defining by an unknown would be nonsensical. Therefore, the first 'tasawwur' cannot mean 'acquisition from ignorance' (which would imply it was unknown), but only 'occurrence in the mind' (خطور بالبال).
The definiens is like a tool that must be available and clear.
4
Understand why the second 'tasawwur' means knowledge after ignorance
The definiendum must be unknown at the start of definition, otherwise defining it would be 'تحصيل الحاصل' (attaining the already attained). Hence the second 'tasawwur' refers to the acquisition of knowledge after ignorance.
This ensures the definition actually informs rather than repeats.
5
Recognise the conclusion that definiens and definiendum are distinct
Bajuri concludes that the two terms are different both in word and in meaning, considering conciseness vs. elaboration in hadd/rasm, and clarity vs. obscurity in verbal definition.
This distinction safeguards against circular definitions.

فَصْلٌ فِي الْمُعَرَّفَاتِ. قَوْلُهُ : (فِي المُعَرِّفَاتِ جَمْعُ: «مُعَرِّف) - بِكَسْرِ الرَّاءِ ، وَهُوَ : مَا يَقْتَضِي تَصَوُّرُهُ تَصَوُّرُ المَعرَّفِ بفتح الرَّاء - ، وَامْتِيَازُه عَنْ غَيْرِهِ» ; فَالأَوَّلُ : الحَدُّ التّامُ، وَالثَّاني : مَا عَدَاهُ مِمَّا سَيَأْتِي وَالمُرَادُ بِـ التَّصَوُّرِ الأَوَّلِ : الخُطُورُ بِالبَالِ، لَا الحُصُولُ عَنْ جَهْلٍ؛ لِأَنَّ المُعَرِّفَ - بِكَسْرِ الرَّاءِ - يَجِبُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعْلُوماً حَالَ التَّعْرِيفِ بِهِ ، وَإِلَّا لَزِمَ التَّعْرِيفُ بِالمَجْهُولِ . وبِ التَّصَوُّرِ الثَّانِي : الحُصُولُ عَنْ جَهْلٍ، لَا الخُطُورُ بِالبَالِ; لأَنَّ المُعَرَّفَ - بِفَتْحِ الرَّاءِ - يَجِبُ أَنْ يَكُونَ مَجْهُولاً حَالَ تَعْرِيفِهِ، وَإِلَّا لَزِمَ تَحْصِيلُ الحَاصِلِ. وَعُلِمَ مِنَ التَّعْرِيفِ المَذْكُورِ : أَنَّ المُعَرِّف - بِالكَسْرِ - غَيْرُ المَعَرَّف - بِالفَتْحِ ، وَهُوَ ظَاهِرُ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلَّفْظِ، وَكَذَا بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلمَعْنَى بِاعْتِبَارِ الإِجْمَالِ وَالتَّفْصِيلِ فِي الحَدِ وَالرَّسْمِ، وَبِاعْتِبَارِ الظُّهُورِ وَالخَفَاءِ فِي التَّعْرِيفِ اللَّفْظِيِّ، فَلْيُتَأَمَّلْ.
Section on definientia. His statement: (في المعرفات) is plural of 'معرف' (with kasr of ra), which is: that whose conception necessitates the conception of the definiendum (with fatha of ra) and its distinction from others. So the first [conception] is the complete definition, and the second is everything besides it as will come. And by the first 'تصور' is meant the occurrence in the mind, not the acquisition from ignorance, because the definiens (with kasr of ra) must be known at the time of defining by it, otherwise defining by an unknown would follow. And by the second 'تصور' is meant the acquisition from ignorance, not the occurrence in the mind, because the definiendum (with fatha of ra) must be unknown at the time of defining it, otherwise the attainment of the attained would follow. And it is known from the mentioned definition that the definiens (with kasr) is other than the definiendum (with fatha). This is apparent with respect to the word, and similarly with respect to the meaning by consideration of conciseness and elaboration in the hadd and rasm, and by consideration of clarity and obscurity in verbal definition. So let it be pondered.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'معرف' (definiens) and clarifies a key precision in the logic of definitions. The author explains that the word 'معرف' (with kasr of ra) refers to that which, when conceived, yields conception of the definiendum (معرف with fatha) and its distinction. He then notes that the first 'تصور' (conception) in the definition means mere mental occurrence (خطور بالبال), not knowledge after ignorance, because the definiens must already be known. The second 'تصور' means knowledge after ignorance, because the definiendum must be unknown. He concludes that from this definition it is clear that the definiens is different from the definiendum, both in word and in meaning, considering conciseness vs. elaboration in essential and accidental definitions, and clarity vs. obscurity in verbal definitions. This distinction prevents the logical error of defining something by itself or using an unknown term.

تَصَوُّر
خُطُورُ بِالبَالِ
حُصُولُ عَنْ جَهْلٍ

Checkpoint
According to Bajuri, why must the first 'tasawwur' be interpreted as 'mere mental occurrence' rather than 'acquisition from ignorance'?
A) Because the definiens must be known at the time of definition, otherwise defining by an unknown would occur.
B) Because the definiendum must be unknown at the time of definition.
C) Because the definiens is always a simple concept.
D) Because the definition must be concise.

Key Takeaway
In a valid definition, the definiens must be conceived as a mere mental occurrence (known), while the definiendum is conceived as an acquisition from ignorance (unknown); this distinction prevents circular or futile definitions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Take a definition from an Islamic science text (e.g., al-Jurjani's definitions in Kitab al-Ta'rifat). For each definition, identify the definiens and definiendum, and explain how the first 'tasawwur' (mental occurrence) applies to the definiens and the second (knowledge after ignorance) applies to the definiendum.
?
Construct a definition for an Islamic legal term (e.g., 'salah' or 'zakat') following the pattern: definiens must be known, definiendum unknown. Then check if your definition would be considered valid according to Bajuri's conditions.

The Three Types of Definitions in Islamic Logic
Bajuri explains the matn's three types and introduces additional types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of definitions (hadd, rasm, lafzi) and list the two additional types some scholars propose (example and division).

Core Idea
Definitions are either by essence, by accident, or verbal, but example and division are not separate.

The matn states three types of definitions. Some scholars add definition by example and definition by division. This lesson helps you understand these basic categories and the debate around them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types from the matn.
The matn says 'hadd, rasm, lafzi'. Hadd is definition by essence, rasm by accident, lafzi verbal.
2
Note the added types by some scholars.
They add ta'rif bi al-mithal (example) and ta'rif bi al-taqsim (division).
3
Observe that the commentator argues they fall under rasm.
They are based on a property of the defined thing, making them types of rasm.
4
Recognize the final binary division.
The true division is only hadd and rasm, with lafzi also considered a type of rasm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُعَرِّفٌ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةٍ قُسِمْ حَدٌ، وَرَسْمِيَّ، وَلَفْظِيٌّ عُلِـمْ. قَوْلُهُ : (مُعَرِّفٌ مُبْتَدَأَ ، وَالمُسَوِّغُ : وُقُوعُهُ فِي مَعْرِضِ التَّفْصِيلِ، وَقَالَ المُصَنِّفُ فِي شَرْحِهِ» : إِنَّهُ حُذِفَتْ مِنْهُ «أَلْ» لِلضَّرُورَةِ. قَوْلُهُ : ( عَلَى ثَلَاثَةٍ قُسِمْ) وَزَادَ بَعْضُهُمْ : التَّعْرِيفَ بِالمِثَالِ ؛ كَقَوْلِهِمْ : العِلْمُ كَالنُّوْرِ، وَالجَهْلُ كَالظُّلْمَةِ». وَالتَّعْرِيفَ بِالتَّقْسِيمِ» ؛ كَقَوْلِهِمْ : «العِلْمُ : تَصَوُّرٌ، أَوْ تَصْدِيقٌ». وَالتَّحْقِيقُ : أَنَّ كُلًّا مِنْهُمَا كَالتَّعْرِيفِ اللَّفْظِيّ دَاخِلٌ فِي الرَّسْمِ ; لِأَنَّهُ مِنَ التَّعْرِيفِ بِالخَاصَّةِ، فَإِنَّ مُشَابَهَةَ العِلْمِ لِلنُّورِ خَاصَّةٌ مِنْ خَوَاصِهِ، وَكَذَا مُشَابَهَةُ الجَهْلِ لِلظُّلْمَةِ، وَانْقِسَامُ الشَّيْءِ إِلَى أَقْسَامِهِ خَاصَّةٌ مِنْ خَوَاصِهِ، وَكَذَلِكَ لَفْظُ القَمْح مَثَلاً فِي تَعْرِيفِ البُرِّ) بِـ: «أَنَّهُ القَمْحُ»، وَعَلَى هَذَا : فَالمُعَرِّفُ عَلَى قِسْمَيْنِ فَقَط ، فَتَكُونُ القِسْمَةُ تُنَائِيَّةٌ ، لَا ثُلاثِيَّةٌ كَمَا فَعَلَ المُصَنِّفُ، فَافْهَمْ. قَوْلُهُ : (حَدٌ) أَيْ: تَامٌ وَنَاقِصٌ وَكَذَا قَوْلُهُ : وَرَسْمِيٌّ»، كَمَا يُعْلَمُ مِمَّا يَأْتِي.
Definiens is divided into three: hadd (definition by essence), rasm (definition by accident), and lafzi (verbal definition). His statement: 'Definiens' is a subject, and the justification [for its being indefinite] is its occurrence in the context of detailing. The author said in his commentary: 'al-' was dropped from it for necessity. His statement: 'divided into three' - Some added definition by example, like their saying: 'Knowledge is like light, ignorance is like darkness', and definition by division, like their saying: 'Knowledge is conception or assent'. And the verification is that each of them is like verbal definition, entering into rasm, because it is definition by a property. For the similarity of knowledge to light is one of its properties, and similarly the similarity of ignorance to darkness, and the division of a thing into its parts is one of its properties. Likewise the word 'wheat' for example in defining 'barley' as 'it is wheat'. And based on this, the definiens is only two divisions, so the division is binary, not ternary as the author did. So understand. His statement: 'hadd' means complete and incomplete, and similarly his statement 'rasm', as will be known from what follows.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage addresses the classification of definitions. The matn states three types: hadd (definition by essence), rasm (definition by accident), and lafzi (verbal definition). The commentator then notes that some scholars add two more: definition by example (مثال) and definition by division (تقسيم). However, the correct position (تحقيق) is that both of these are actually subsumed under rasm, because they rely on a specific property of the defined thing. For instance, likening knowledge to light is a property of knowledge, and dividing knowledge into conception and assent is also a property. Similarly, defining 'barley' as 'wheat' is a verbal definition with synonymy, also a property. Thus, the true division of definitions is only two: hadd and rasm, while lafzi is considered a form of rasm? Actually the commentator says that example and division are like lafzi and fall under rasm. He concludes that the division is binary, not ternary. He also clarifies that hadd includes both complete and incomplete, and rasm similarly.

رسم
تعريف لفظي
تعريف بالمثال
تعريف بالتقسيم

Key Takeaway
Definitions in Islamic logic are fundamentally two: hadd (essential) and rasm (accidental); other forms like example and division are subtypes of rasm.

The Binary Division of Definitions and the Role of Property
Bajuri provides the verification that example and division are part of rasm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why definition by example and definition by division are considered types of rasm based on the concept of property (khassa).

Core Idea
Any definition that relies on a non-essential property is a rasm, so example and division fall under it.

The commentator argues that example and division are not independent definitions; they are rasm because they use a specific property of the thing defined. Understanding what counts as a property is key.

Guided Path
1
Identify the examples given.
Knowledge like light, division into parts, synonym 'wheat'. These are the examples of added types.
2
Notice that each relies on a property.
The commentator says 'similarity of knowledge to light is one of its properties'.
3
Understand that property (خاصة) is a non-essential characteristic.
A property is not part of the essence; it is an accidental attribute.
4
Conclude that any definition using such a property is a rasm.
Since the definition uses a property, it cannot be a hadd (essential definition); hence it falls under rasm.

Hadd and Rasm

The True Division of Definitions: Hadd and Rasm
Commentary on definition classification with reduction to two types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given definition as hadd, rasm, or a subtype of rasm, and explain why definition by example and division are not separate types.

Core Idea
The only genuine types of definition are essential (hadd) and descriptive (rasm); all others are subsumed under rasm.

In this passage, al-Bajuri unpacks a verse that divides definitions into three types. He then makes a crucial logical move: he shows that additional proposed types—definition by example and by division—are actually forms of descriptive definition (rasm). This reduces the division to a binary one. Understanding why some definitions are really rasm is key to using definitions correctly in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish 'definer' from 'defined'
Al-Bajuri begins by noting the difference in vowelization: mu'arif (with kasr, the definer) vs. mu'arraf (with fatha, the defined). This is a terminological clarification that sets the stage.
Not essential for the classification but shows precision.
2
Identify the three types from the verse
The original verse lists three: hadd (complete definition with genus and differentia), rasm (descriptive definition with genus and accident), and ta'rīf lafẓī (verbal definition, explaining a word by a familiar synonym). These are the starting point.
3
Understand the proposed additional types
Some scholars added definition by example (tamthīl) and definition by division (taqsīm). For example, 'knowledge is like light' or 'knowledge is concept or assent'. Al-Bajuri explains that these are not independent.
Recognize that these are common in theological and juristic discourse.
4
Learn the verification (tahqīq) reduction
Al-Bajuri argues that both definition by example and division rely on a special characteristic (khāṣṣa) of the thing, not its essence. Therefore they fall under rasm, which also uses non-essential properties. Similarly, verbal definition is a rasm because it uses a synonym—a special relationship between words. Thus the true division is binary: hadd and rasm.
This is the key logical move: showing that what seemed like additional types are actually subtypes of rasm.

فصل في المعرفات (٤٠) مُعَرِّفٌ عَلَى ثَلَاثَةٍ قُسِمْ حَدٌ، وَرَسْمِيَّ، وَلَفْظِيٌّ عُلِـمْ الباجوري وَعُلِمَ مِنَ التَّعْرِيفِ المَذْكُورِ : أَنَّ المُعَرِّف - بِالكَسْرِ - غَيْرُ المَعَرَّف - بِالفَتْحِ ، وَهُوَ ظَاهِرُ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلَّفْظِ، وَكَذَا بِالنِّسْبَةِ لِلمَعْنَى بِاعْتِبَارِ الإِجْمَالِ وَالتَّفْصِيلِ فِي الحَدٌ وَالرَّسْمِ، وَبِاعْتِبَارِ الظُّهُورِ وَالخَفَاءِ فِي التَّعْرِيفِ اللَّفْظِيِّ، فَلْيُتَأَمَّلْ. قَوْلُهُ : (مُعَرِّفٌ مُبْتَدَأَ ، وَالمُسَوِّغُ : وُقُوعُهُ فِي مَعْرِضِ التَّفْصِيلِ، وَقَالَ المُصَنِّفُ فِي شَرْحِهِ : إِنَّهُ حُذِفَتْ مِنْهُ «أَلْ» لِلضَّرُورَةِ قَوْلُهُ : ( عَلَى ثَلَاثَةٍ قُسِمْ) وَزَادَ بَعْضُهُمْ : التَّعْرِيفَ بِالمِثَالِ ؛ كَقَوْلِهِمْ : العِلْمُ كَالنُّوْرِ، وَالجَهْلُ كَالظُّلْمَةِ. وَالتَّعْرِيفَ بِالتَّقْسِيمِ ؛ كَقَوْلِهِمْ : «العِلْمُ : تَصَوُّرٌ، أَوْ تَصْدِيقٌ». وَالتَّحْقِيقُ : أَنَّ كُلًّا مِنْهُمَا كَالتَّعْرِيفِ اللَّفْظِيِّ دَاخِلٌ فِي الرَّسْمِ ; لِأَنَّهُ مِنَ التَّعْرِيفِ بِالخَاصَّةِ، فَإِنَّ مُشَابَهَةَ العِلْمِ لِلنُّورِ خَاصَّةٌ مِنْ خَوَاصٍّهِ، وَكَذَا مُشَابَهَةُ الجَهْلِ لِلظُّلْمَةِ، وَانْقِسَامُ الشَّيْءِ إِلَى أَقْسَامِهِ خَاصَّةٌ مِنْ خَوَاصٍّهِ، وَكَذَلِكَ لَفْظُ القَمْح مَثَلاً فِي تَعْرِيفِ البُرِّ) بِـ: «أَنَّهُ القَمْحُ»، وَعَلَى هَذَا : فَالمُعَرِّفُ عَلَى قِسْمَيْنِ فَقَط ، فَتَكُونُ القِسْمَةُ تُنَائِيَّةٌ ، لَا ثُلاثِيَّةٌ كَمَا فَعَلَ المُصَنِّفُ، فَافْهَمْ.
Section on definitions. (40) A definer is divided into three: complete definition, descriptive definition, and verbal definition—it is known. Al-Bajuri said: And it is known from the mentioned definition that the definer (with kasr) is other than the defined (with fatha), and this is apparent with respect to the word, and likewise with respect to the meaning in consideration of summarization and elaboration in the complete and descriptive definition, and in consideration of clarity and obscurity in the verbal definition, so reflect. His statement: (A definer) is a subject, and the justification is its occurrence in the context of elaboration, and the author said in his commentary that the 'alif lam' was omitted from it due to necessity. His statement: (Divided into three) and some added: definition by example, like their saying: knowledge is like light, and ignorance is like darkness; and definition by division, like their saying: knowledge is concept or assent. And the verification is that both, like the verbal definition, are included in the descriptive definition, because it is from definition by a special characteristic, for the resemblance of knowledge to light is a special characteristic of it, and likewise the resemblance of ignorance to darkness, and the division of a thing into its parts is a special characteristic of it, and similarly the word 'wheat' for example in defining 'barley' by: 'it is wheat'. And on this basis, the definer is only two kinds, so the division is binary, not ternary as the author did, so understand.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a verse that classifies definitions. The author, al-Bajuri, begins by distinguishing between the definer (mu'arif) and the defined (mu'arraf), noting the difference in vowelization. He then elaborates on the three types mentioned in the verse: hadd (complete definition), rasm (descriptive definition), and lafdhi (verbal definition). He explains that some scholars add two more types: definition by example (tamthil) and definition by division (taqsim). However, the verified position (tahqiq) is that these two are actually subsumed under rasm because they rely on a special characteristic (khassa) of the thing defined. For instance, comparing knowledge to light is a special property of knowledge, not its essence. Similarly, dividing knowledge into concept and assent is a property of knowledge. Therefore, the true division is only into two types: hadd and rasm. The verbal definition is also part of rasm. The author warns the student to understand this reduction, as the original verse's ternary division is not the final word.

Key Terms
مُعَرِّف
حَدّ
رَسْم
تَعْرِيف لَفْظِي

Checkpoint
According to al-Bajuri's verification (tahqiq), how many genuine types of definition are there?
A) Three
B) Two
C) Four
D) One

Key Takeaway
The essential classification of definitions is binary: essential (hadd) and descriptive (rasm); all other forms are subtypes of rasm because they rely on non-essential properties.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Look up the definition of 'wudu' in a fiqh manual. Is it a hadd or a rasm? Identify the genus and differentia if it is a hadd, or the special characteristic if it is a rasm.
?
A scholar defines 'iman' as 'belief in the heart, speech on the tongue, and action of the limbs.' Classify this definition according to al-Bajuri's scheme. Is it a hadd, rasm, or something else? Justify your answer using the concept of khassa.

Hadd and Rasm
beginner
5 min
Hadd and Rasm: Components and Proximity
Author defines hadd and rasm and emphasizes proximate terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hadd and rasm and explain why the genus and differentia must be proximate.

Core Idea
Hadd needs proximate genus and differentia; rasm uses genus and accident.

In this passage, Al-Bajuri breaks down the two types of definition: complete (hadd) and descriptive (rasm). He emphasizes that the genus and differentia used must be proximate—that is, the immediate category and the specific difference—to accurately capture the essence of the defined term.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
From the verse, extract what makes up a complete definition (hadd) and a descriptive definition (rasm).
The verse says: 'al-hadd bi al-jinsi wa fadlin waqa'a wa al-rasmu bi al-jinsi wa khassatin ma'a.'
2
List the components
Hadd has genus and differentia; rasm has genus and accident.
Note that rasm uses an accident (khassa) instead of differentia.
3
Understand the requirement of proximity
Al-Bajuri specifies that the genus must be proximate (qarib) and the differentia must also be proximate. He explains that mentioning a distant genus or differentia is not beneficial because it is either more general or equal to the proximate term.
Example: 'growing' (al-nami) is too broad to serve as differentia for human; 'animal' is the proximate genus.
4
Apply the distinction
Given a definition, test whether it uses proximate terms and classify it as hadd or rasm.
For instance, 'Human is a rational animal' is a hadd because animal is proximate genus and rational is proximate differentia.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَـ «الحَدُّ بِـ : الجِنْسِ وَفَضْلٍ وَقَعَا وَالرَّسْمُ» بـ : الجِنْسِ وَخَاصَةٍ مَعَا الباجوري وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ الحَدَّ فِي اللُّغَةِ : المَنْعُ ; أُطْلِقَ عَلَى مَا يَأْتِي ; لِمَنْعِهِ مِنْ دُخُولِ أَفْرَادِ غَيْرِ المُعَرَّفِ فِيهِ، وَمِنْ خُرُوجِ أَفْرَادِهِ مِنْهُ. لا يُقَالُ: يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُسَمَّى الرَّسْمُ : «حَدَّا»; لِمَنْعِهِ مِنْ ذَلِكَ . لأَنَّا نَقُولُ : مَنْعُ الرَّسْمِ ضَعِيفٌ فَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ; عَلَى أَنَّ وَجْهَ التَّسْمِيَةِ لَا يُوجِبُهَا ، كَمَا هُوَ مَشْهُورٌ . قَوْلُهُ : (وَرَسْمِيٌّ) وَيُقَالُ لَهُ : رَسْمٌ» أَيْضاً . فَإِنْ قِيلَ : يَلْزَمُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ نِسْبَةُ الشَّيْءِ إِلَى نَفْسِهِ ; لِأَنَّهُ مَنْسُوبٌ لِلرَّسْمِ الَّذِي هُوَ هُوَ . أُجِيبَ : بِأَنَّهُ مَنْسُوبٌ لِلرَّسْمِ اللُّغَوِيّ ( وَهُوَ : الأَثَرُ»، لا المُصْطَلَحِ عَلَيْهِ حَتَّى يَلْزَمَ مَا ذُكِرَ. قَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ : وَيُمْكِنُ أَنْ يُتَكَلَّفُ بِأَنْ يُقَالَ : إِنَّهُ مَنْسُوبٌ لِلرَّسْمِ المُصْطَلَحِ عَلَيْهِ، وَيُرَادُ مِنْهُ فَرْدٌ مِنْ أَفْرَادِهِ، فَيَكُونُ مِنْ نِسْبَةِ النَّوْعِ إِلَى فَرْدِهِ . قَوْلُهُ : (وَلَفْظِيٌّ) مَنْسُوبٌ لِلَّفْظِ ، مِنْ نِسْبَةِ الخَاصٌ لِلعَامّ، وَقَدْ عَرَفْتَ أَنَّهُ لَا حَاجَةَ لِزِيَادَةِ ذَلِكَ عَلَى التَّحْقِيقِ، فَلَا تَغْفَلُ . قَوْلُهُ : (عُلِمْ) تَكْمِلَةٌ لِلبَيْتِ، وَكَأَنَّهُ نَبَّهَ بِهِ عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ اللَّفْظُ المُعَرَّفُ بِهِ عُلِمَ مَعْنَاهُ، وَإِنَّمَا جُهِلَ كَوْنُهُ مُسَمًّى بِاللَّفْظ الآخَرِ ; أَفَادَهُ ابْنُ يَعْقُوبَ. قَوْلُهُ : (فَـ «الحَدُّ» بـ: الجِنْسِ... إلخ) «الفَاءُ لِلإِفصاح ; لِأَنَّهَا أَفْصَحَتْ عَنْ شَرْطٍ مَحْذُوفٍ، وَالتَّقْدِيرُ : إِذَا أَرَدْتَ بَيَانَ ذَلِكَ، فَالحَدُّ ... إلخ»، وَمُرَادُهُ : بَيَانُ الحَدِّ التَّام . وَأَرَادَ بِـ «الجِنْسِ»: الجِنْسَ القَرِيبَ ، كَمَا يُؤخَذُ مِنْ قَوْلِهِ : «وَنَاقِصُ الحَدِّ ... إلخ» . وَقَوْلُهُ : (وَفَضْلٍ ) أَيْ: قَرِيبٍ ; لِأَنَّ ذِكْرَ البَعِيدِ بَعْدَ الجِنْسِ القَرِيبِ لَا يُفِيدُ; لِأَنَّهُ إِمَّا أَعَمُّ مِنْهُ أَوْ مُسَاوِ لَهُ كَـ: «النَّامِي» و«الحَسَّاسِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لـ «الحَيَوَانِ».
Thus, the complete definition is by the genus and a differentia, and the descriptive definition is by the genus and an accident together. Al-Bajuri said: And know that 'hadd' in language is 'prevention'; it is applied to what follows because it prevents the entry of individuals of what is not defined into it, and prevents the exit of its individuals from it. It cannot be said: the descriptive definition should be called 'hadd' because it also prevents that. Because we say: the prevention by descriptive definition is weak so it is not considered; moreover, the reason for naming does not necessitate it, as is well-known. His statement: (And descriptive definition) and it is also called 'rasm'. If it is said: this necessitates attributing a thing to itself because it is attributed to 'rasm' which is itself. The answer: it is attributed to the linguistic 'rasm' which is 'effect', not the technical term, so the mentioned consequence does not follow. Some said: it is possible to say with effort that it is attributed to the technical 'rasm', intending an individual of its individuals, so it is a relation of the species to its individual. His statement: (And verbal definition) is attributed to the word, from the relation of the specific to the general, and you have known that there is no need for its addition according to verification, so do not neglect. His statement: (It is known) is a completion of the verse, and it seems he alerted that the word by which definition is made must have its meaning known, and only its being a name for another word is unknown; as stated by Ibn Ya'qub. His statement: (Thus, the complete definition is by the genus... etc.) The 'fa' is for clarification, because it clarifies an omitted condition, the estimation: if you want to explain that, then the complete definition... etc. And he intends by 'genus' the proximate genus, as understood from his statement: 'and the incomplete definition... etc.' And his statement: (and a differentia) meaning proximate; because mentioning the distant after the proximate genus is not beneficial; because it is either more general than it or equal to it, like 'growing' and 'sensing' in relation to 'animal'.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage defines the two fundamental types of definition: hadd (complete definition) and rasm (descriptive definition). The author begins by explaining the linguistic meaning of 'hadd' as 'prevention', and why it is applied to the technical term: it prevents both the inclusion of what is not part of the definition and the exclusion of what is. He then addresses a possible objection: if rasm also prevents this, why is it not called 'hadd'? The answer is that rasm's prevention is weak, and the reason for naming does not force the term. Next, he discusses the term 'rasmi', explaining that it is attributed to 'rasm'. A subtle objection is raised: if 'rasmi' means 'pertaining to rasm', then it is a self-reference, since 'rasm' itself is the same term. The solution is that the attribution is to the linguistic meaning of 'rasm' as 'effect', not to the technical term, or alternatively, it is a relation of the species to an individual. He then comments on 'lafdhi' (verbal definition), noting it is a relation of the specific to the general. Following that, he explains 'ulima' (known), emphasizing that the defining word must be known in meaning, but its being a name for another word may be unknown. Finally, he breaks down the verse, explaining that 'fa' clarifies a condition, and that 'jins' refers to the proximate genus, and 'fadl' to the proximate differentia. He gives the example: 'growing' and 'sensing' are too broad compared to 'animal', so they cannot be the differentia.

Key Takeaway

?

Hadd and Rasm

Objections and Refinements: Rasm, Rasmi, and Ulima
Author addresses objections and clarifies terms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why rasm is not called hadd, how the term 'rasmi' avoids self-reference, and what condition 'ulima' adds.

Core Idea
Rasm's prevention is weak; 'rasmi' refers to linguistic meaning; 'ulima' ensures the definer knows the meaning.

After defining the types, Al-Bajuri addresses several objections and clarifies terminology. He answers why rasm is not considered a complete definition, resolves the apparent self-reference in 'rasmi', and explains the necessity of knowing the meaning of the defining word.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection against rasm
Someone might say: since rasm also prevents confusion like hadd, why isn't it called hadd? Locate this in the text.
The text: 'La yuqalu: yanbaghi an yusamma al-rasmu haddan; liman'ihi min dhalika.'
2
Follow Al-Bajuri's answer
He says the prevention by rasm is weak (da'if) and therefore not considered. Moreover, the reason for naming does not necessitate the name.
He adds: 'man'u al-rasmi da'ifun fala yu'tabaru.'
3
Understand the self-reference issue with 'rasmi'
The term 'rasmi' (attributed to rasm) seems to attribute a thing to itself. The solution: it refers to the linguistic meaning of rasm (effect), not the technical term.
Alternatively, it could be analyzed as a relation of the species to an individual.
4
Grasp the condition 'ulima'
The word 'ulima' (known) is part of the definition: the defining word must have a known meaning; only its being a name for another word is unknown.
Ibn Ya'qub clarified this.

فَـ «الحَدُّ بِـ : الجِنْسِ وَفَضْلٍ وَقَعَا وَالرَّسْمُ» بـ : الجِنْسِ وَخَاصَةٍ مَعَا الباجوري وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّ الحَدَّ فِي اللُّغَةِ : المَنْعُ ; أُطْلِقَ عَلَى مَا يَأْتِي ; لِمَنْعِهِ مِنْ دُخُولِ أَفْرَادِ غَيْرِ المُعَرَّفِ فِيهِ، وَمِنْ خُرُوجِ أَفْرَادِهِ مِنْهُ. لا يُقَالُ: يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يُسَمَّى الرَّسْمُ : «حَدَّا»; لِمَنْعِهِ مِنْ ذَلِكَ . لأَنَّا نَقُولُ : مَنْعُ الرَّسْمِ ضَعِيفٌ فَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ; عَلَى أَنَّ وَجْهَ التَّسْمِيَةِ لَا يُوجِبُهَا ، كَمَا هُوَ مَشْهُورٌ . قَوْلُهُ : (وَرَسْمِيٌّ) وَيُقَالُ لَهُ : رَسْمٌ» أَيْضاً . فَإِنْ قِيلَ : يَلْزَمُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ نِسْبَةُ الشَّيْءِ إِلَى نَفْسِهِ ; لِأَنَّهُ مَنْسُوبٌ لِلرَّسْمِ الَّذِي هُوَ هُوَ . أُجِيبَ : بِأَنَّهُ مَنْسُوبٌ لِلرَّسْمِ اللُّغَوِيّ ( وَهُوَ : الأَثَرُ»، لا المُصْطَلَحِ عَلَيْهِ حَتَّى يَلْزَمَ مَا ذُكِرَ. قَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ : وَيُمْكِنُ أَنْ يُتَكَلَّفُ بِأَنْ يُقَالَ : إِنَّهُ مَنْسُوبٌ لِلرَّسْمِ المُصْطَلَحِ عَلَيْهِ، وَيُرَادُ مِنْهُ فَرْدٌ مِنْ أَفْرَادِهِ، فَيَكُونُ مِنْ نِسْبَةِ النَّوْعِ إِلَى فَرْدِهِ . قَوْلُهُ : (وَلَفْظِيٌّ) مَنْسُوبٌ لِلَّفْظِ ، مِنْ نِسْبَةِ الخَاصٌ لِلعَامّ، وَقَدْ عَرَفْتَ أَنَّهُ لَا حَاجَةَ لِزِيَادَةِ ذَلِكَ عَلَى التَّحْقِيقِ، فَلَا تَغْفَلُ . قَوْلُهُ : (عُلِمْ) تَكْمِلَةٌ لِلبَيْتِ، وَكَأَنَّهُ نَبَّهَ بِهِ عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ اللَّفْظُ المُعَرَّفُ بِهِ عُلِمَ مَعْنَاهُ، وَإِنَّمَا جُهِلَ كَوْنُهُ مُسَمًّى بِاللَّفْظ الآخَرِ ; أَفَادَهُ ابْنُ يَعْقُوبَ. قَوْلُهُ : (فَـ «الحَدُّ» بـ: الجِنْسِ... إلخ) «الفَاءُ لِلإِفصاح ; لِأَنَّهَا أَفْصَحَتْ عَنْ شَرْطٍ مَحْذُوفٍ، وَالتَّقْدِيرُ : إِذَا أَرَدْتَ بَيَانَ ذَلِكَ، فَالحَدُّ ... إلخ»، وَمُرَادُهُ : بَيَانُ الحَدِّ التَّام . وَأَرَادَ بِـ «الجِنْسِ»: الجِنْسَ القَرِيبَ ، كَمَا يُؤخَذُ مِنْ قَوْلِهِ : «وَنَاقِصُ الحَدِّ ... إلخ» . وَقَوْلُهُ : (وَفَضْلٍ ) أَيْ: قَرِيبٍ ; لِأَنَّ ذِكْرَ البَعِيدِ بَعْدَ الجِنْسِ القَرِيبِ لَا يُفِيدُ; لِأَنَّهُ إِمَّا أَعَمُّ مِنْهُ أَوْ مُسَاوِ لَهُ كَـ: «النَّامِي» و«الحَسَّاسِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لـ «الحَيَوَانِ».
Thus, the complete definition is by the genus and a differentia, and the descriptive definition is by the genus and an accident together. Al-Bajuri said: And know that 'hadd' in language is 'prevention'; it is applied to what follows because it prevents the entry of individuals of what is not defined into it, and prevents the exit of its individuals from it. It cannot be said: the descriptive definition should be called 'hadd' because it also prevents that. Because we say: the prevention by descriptive definition is weak so it is not considered; moreover, the reason for naming does not necessitate it, as is well-known. His statement: (And descriptive definition) and it is also called 'rasm'. If it is said: this necessitates attributing a thing to itself because it is attributed to 'rasm' which is itself. The answer: it is attributed to the linguistic 'rasm' which is 'effect', not the technical term, so the mentioned consequence does not follow. Some said: it is possible to say with effort that it is attributed to the technical 'rasm', intending an individual of its individuals, so it is a relation of the species to its individual. His statement: (And verbal definition) is attributed to the word, from the relation of the specific to the general, and you have known that there is no need for its addition according to verification, so do not neglect. His statement: (It is known) is a completion of the verse, and it seems he alerted that the word by which definition is made must have its meaning known, and only its being a name for another word is unknown; as stated by Ibn Ya'qub. His statement: (Thus, the complete definition is by the genus... etc.) The 'fa' is for clarification, because it clarifies an omitted condition, the estimation: if you want to explain that, then the complete definition... etc. And he intends by 'genus' the proximate genus, as understood from his statement: 'and the incomplete definition... etc.' And his statement: (and a differentia) meaning proximate; because mentioning the distant after the proximate genus is not beneficial; because it is either more general than it or equal to it, like 'growing' and 'sensing' in relation to 'animal'.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage defines the two fundamental types of definition: hadd (complete definition) and rasm (descriptive definition). The author begins by explaining the linguistic meaning of 'hadd' as 'prevention', and why it is applied to the technical term: it prevents both the inclusion of what is not part of the definition and the exclusion of what is. He then addresses a possible objection: if rasm also prevents this, why is it not called 'hadd'? The answer is that rasm's prevention is weak, and the reason for naming does not force the term. Next, he discusses the term 'rasmi', explaining that it is attributed to 'rasm'. A subtle objection is raised: if 'rasmi' means 'pertaining to rasm', then it is a self-reference, since 'rasm' itself is the same term. The solution is that the attribution is to the linguistic meaning of 'rasm' as 'effect', not to the technical term, or alternatively, it is a relation of the species to an individual. He then comments on 'lafdhi' (verbal definition), noting it is a relation of the specific to the general. Following that, he explains 'ulima' (known), emphasizing that the defining word must be known in meaning, but its being a name for another word may be unknown. Finally, he breaks down the verse, explaining that 'fa' clarifies a condition, and that 'jins' refers to the proximate genus, and 'fadl' to the proximate differentia. He gives the example: 'growing' and 'sensing' are too broad compared to 'animal', so they cannot be the differentia.

Key Terms
رَسْم
رَسْمِيّ
لَفْظِيّ
عُلِم

According to Al-Bajuri, why is 'rasmi' not a self-reference?
A) Because it refers to the linguistic meaning of 'rasm' as effect.
B) Because it is an attribute of God.
C) Because it is a metaphorical usage.
D) Because it is a type of hadd.

Key Takeaway
Rasm is not called hadd due to weak prevention; 'rasmi' avoids self-reference by referring to the linguistic meaning; 'ulima' ensures the definer knows the meaning of the term.

Hadd and Rasm
intermediate
5 min
Components of Complete Hadd and Rasm, and Their Incomplete Forms
Author details the components of complete hadd and rasm, and incomplete forms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the components of a complete essential definition (hadd tamm) and a complete descriptive definition (rasm tamm), and distinguish incomplete forms by recognizing missing or misplaced elements.

Core Idea
A complete definition requires the right components in the right order; incomplete definitions are missing a necessary part or using a distant genus.

In this passage, the commentator explains the precise ingredients for a complete definition (hadd) and a complete description (rasm), and also the forms of incomplete definitions. You already know that definitions contain a genus and a differentia or property. Now you will learn the critical conditions: the genus must be proximate, the differentia close, the property comprehensive and constant, and the order matters. This will sharpen your ability to evaluate definitions found in Islamic scientific works.

Guided Path
1
Identify complete hadd components
From the matn: 'al-hadd bi al-jins wa fasl'. The commentary specifies that the genus must be proximate (jins qarib) and the differentia close (fasl qarib). The example of 'growing' and 'sensing' for 'animal' shows redundancy if distant.
2
Identify complete rasm components
'al-rasm bi al-jins wa khassa'. The commentary adds conditions: the property (khassa) must be comprehensive (shamila) and constant (lazima). Also the genus must precede the property. Examples: 'knowledgeable' for man (non-comprehensive) and 'actually breathing' for animal (non-constant).
3
Recognize incomplete hadd forms
Two forms: (1) by differentia alone, e.g., 'Man is rational' (missing genus); (2) by differentia with distant genus, e.g., 'Man is a rational body' (using 'body' instead of 'animal').
In the second form, a distant genus is still a genus but not the proximate one.
4
Understand order in rasm
In complete rasm, the genus must come before the property; otherwise it becomes incomplete rasm. This is an additional condition beyond having both components.
