قَوْلُهُ : (فَـ «الحَدُّ» بـ: الجِنْسِ... إلخ) «الفَاءُ لِلإِفصاح ; لِأَنَّهَا أَفْصَحَتْ عَنْ شَرْطٍ مَحْذُوفٍ، وَالتَّقْدِيرُ : إِذَا أَرَدْتَ بَيَانَ ذَلِكَ، فَالحَدُّ ... إلخ»، وَمُرَادُهُ : بَيَانُ الحَدِّ التَّام .
وَأَرَادَ بِـ «الجِنْسِ»: الجِنْسَ القَرِيبَ ، كَمَا يُؤخَذُ مِنْ قَوْلِهِ : «وَنَاقِصُ الحَدِّ ... إلخ» . وَقَوْلُهُ : (وَفَضْلٍ ) أَيْ: قَرِيبٍ ; لِأَنَّ ذِكْرَ البَعِيدِ بَعْدَ الجِنْسِ القَرِيبِ لَا يُفِيدُ; لِأَنَّهُ إِمَّا أَعَمُّ مِنْهُ أَوْ مُسَاوِ لَهُ كَـ: «النَّامِي» و«الحَسَّاسِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لـ «الحَيَوَانِ».
قَوْلُهُ : (وَالرَّسْمُ) أَي : التَّامُ .
وَقَوْلُهُ : (بِـ : الجِنْسِ أَي : القَرِيبِ، كَمَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنْ قَوْلِهِ : «وَنَاقِصُ الرَّسْمِ ... إلخ».
وَقَوْلُهُ : (وَخَاصَةٍ) أَيْ : شَامِلَةٍ لَازِمَةٍ .
بِخِلَافِ غَيْرِ الشَّامِلَةِ كَـ: «العَالِمِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لـ «الإِنْسَانِ، فَلَا يُعَرَّفُ بِهَا; لِخُرُوجِ كَثِيرٍ مِنَ الْأَفْرَادِ عَنْهَا، وَبِخِلَافِ غَيْرِ اللَّازِمَةِ كَـ : المُتَنَفِّسِ بِالفِعْلِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لـ «الحَيَوَانِ»، فَلَا يُعَرَّفُ بِهَا ; لِخُرُوجِ أَفْرَادِ المَحْدُودِ عَنْهَا حَالَ المُفَارَقَةِ .
وَيُشْتَرَطُ فِي تَمَامِ الرَّسْمِ زِيَادَةٌ عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ : تَقْدِيمُ الجِنْسِ عَلَى الخَاصَّةِ، وَإِلَّا كَانَ رَسْماً ناقصاً .
قَوْلُهُ : (مَعَا) أَيْ : حَالَ كَوْنِهِمَا مَعاً .
قَوْلُهُ : (وَنَاقِصُ الحَدٌ ) مِنْ إِضَافَةِ الصِّفَةِ لِلمَوْصُوفِ .
وَقَوْلُهُ : (بِـ : فَصْلِ ... إلخ) ذَكَرَ لِلحَدِّ النَّاقِسِ صُورَتَيْنِ :
(١) - الأُوْلَى : أَنْ يَكُونَ بِالفَصْلِ وَحْدَهُ; كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ : نَاطِقٌ». (۲) - الثَّانِيَةُ : أَنْ يَكُونَ بِالفَصْلِ مَعَ الجِنْسِ البَعِيدِ ; كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ : جِسْمٌ نَاطِقٌ.
So 'the complete definition (hadd)' occurs by [mentioning] the genus and a differentia, and 'the complete descriptive definition (rasm)' by [mentioning] the genus and a property together. And the incomplete definition (hadd) occurs by a differentia alone or together with a distant genus. His saying: ('So the complete definition' by the genus...) The fa' is for explanation, because it explains an implied condition, and the estimation is: When you want to explain that, then the complete definition... etc. And he meant by 'the genus' the proximate genus, as is taken from his saying 'and the incomplete definition...' And his saying: (and a differentia) i.e., a close one; because mentioning the distant after the proximate genus is not useful, because it is either more general than it or equal to it, like 'growing' and 'sensing' in relation to 'animal.' His saying: (and the descriptive definition) i.e., the complete one. And his saying: (by the genus) i.e., the proximate, as taken from his saying 'and the incomplete descriptive definition...' And his saying: (and a property) i.e., comprehensive and constant. Unlike the non-comprehensive, like 'knowledgeable' in relation to 'man,' for one does not define by it because many individuals fall outside it; and unlike the non-constant, like 'actually breathing' in relation to 'animal,' for one does not define by it because individuals of the defined fall outside it at the time of separation. And for the completeness of the descriptive definition, an additional condition beyond what was mentioned: the genus must precede the property, otherwise it would be an incomplete descriptive definition. His saying: (together) i.e., while they are together. His saying: (and the incomplete definition) is a genitive construction of the adjective to the described. And his saying: (by a differentia... etc.) He mentioned two forms for the incomplete definition: First: that it be by the differentia alone, like saying 'Man is rational.' Second: that it be by the differentia together with the distant genus, like saying 'Man is a rational body.'
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the matn lines that specify the components of complete and incomplete definitions. The author explains that a complete essential definition (hadd tamm) must include the proximate genus and a close differentia. The differentia must be 'close' meaning a specific differentia that immediately distinguishes the species; mentioning a distant differentia after a proximate genus is redundant because it would be either coextensive or broader. For example, defining 'animal' as 'growing sentient body' is unnecessary because 'growing' and 'sentient' are already implied in the genus 'body'. For the complete descriptive definition (rasm tamm), the components are the proximate genus and a property (khassa) that is both comprehensive (shamila) and constant (lazima). A property is comprehensive if it applies to all individuals of the species; a non-comprehensive property (like 'knowledgeable' for man) does not cover all, e.g., children. A property is constant if it always accompanies the species; a non-constant property (like 'actually breathing' for animal) may cease. The author also emphasizes that in a complete descriptive definition the genus must precede the property; otherwise it becomes incomplete. For incomplete essential definitions, two forms are given: (1) defining by the differentia alone, e.g., 'Man is rational', which omits the genus; (2) defining by the differentia together with a distant genus, e.g., 'Man is a rational body', which uses 'body' (distant genus) instead of 'animal' (proximate genus).

خاصة

Key Takeaway
A complete definition requires the proximate genus and a close differentia for hadd, or proximate genus and a comprehensive constant property in proper order for rasm; any deviation yields an incomplete form.

Hadd and Rasm

Conditions for a Complete Hadd (Definition)
Bajuri clarifies the ordering condition for complete hadd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate whether a given definition qualifies as a complete hadd by checking the ordering of genus and differentia.

Core Idea
A complete hadd requires the genus to precede the differentia.

This passage from Bajuri's commentary on al-Bannani's matn isolates the key condition for a complete definition (hadd). While a hadd consists of a genus and a differentia, the order matters: the genus must come first, otherwise the definition is incomplete. This condition prevents confusion between the broader category and the specific distinguishing feature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find in the Arabic the term being defined: 'al-hadd al-tamm' (the complete definition). Note that the matn says 'al-hadd bi al-jins wa fasl waqa'a'.
2
Extract the components
A complete hadd consists of a genus (jins) and a differentia (fasl). These two elements must be present.
3
Check the ordering condition
Bajuri states that the genus must precede the differentia. If the differentia comes first, the definition is incomplete (hadd naqis). Look for his phrase 'taqdim al-jins ala al-fasl'.
The order is from broader category (genus) to narrower distinguishing trait.
4
Apply to a sample definition
Take the definition of 'human' as 'animal that laughs'. 'Animal' is the genus, 'that laughs' is the differentia. The genus precedes, so it satisfies the ordering condition.
If the definition were 'laughing animal', the differentia would come first, making it incomplete.

قَوْلُهُ : (وَقَعَا) خَبَرٌ عَنْ قَوْلِهِ : «فَالحَدُّ)، وَالأَلِفُ فِيهِ لِلإِطْلَاقِ.
قَوْلُهُ : (وَالرَّسْمُ) أَي : التَّامُ .
وَقَوْلُهُ : (بِـ : الجِنْسِ أَي : القَرِيبِ، كَمَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنْ قَوْلِهِ : «وَنَاقِصُ الرَّسْمِ ... إلخ».
وَقَوْلُهُ : (وَخَاصَةٍ) أَيْ : شَامِلَةٍ لَازِمَةٍ .
بِخِلَافِ غَيْرِ الشَّامِلَةِ كَـ: «العَالِمِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لـ «الإِنْسَانِ، فَلَا يُعَرَّفُ بِهَا؛ لِخُرُوجِ كَثِيرٍ مِنَ الْأَفْرَادِ عَنْهَا، وَبِخِلَافِ غَيْرِ اللَّازِمَةِ كَـ : المُتَنَفِّسِ بِالفِعْلِ بِالنِّسْبَةِ لـ «الحَيَوَانِ»، فَلَا يُعَرَّفُ بِهَا ؛ لِخُرُوجِ أَفْرَادِ المَحْدُودِ عَنْهَا حَالَ المُفَارَقَةِ .
وَيُشْتَرَطُ فِي تَمَامِ الرَّسْمِ زِيَادَةٌ عَلَى مَا ذُكِرَ : تَقْدِيمُ الجِنْسِ عَلَى الخَاصَّةِ، وَإِلَّا كَانَ رَسْماً ناقصاً ، أَفَادَهُ بَعْضُ المُحَقِّقِينَ)
قَوْلُهُ : (مَعَا) أَيْ : حَالَ كَوْنِهِمَا مَعاً .
Section on Definers. (41) So the complete definition (hadd) is by the genus and a differentia – they occurred. (42) And the complete description (rasm) is by the genus and a property together. Al-Bajuri said: And it is required for the completeness of the definition, in addition to what is understood from what has passed, the precedence of the genus over the differentia. Otherwise, it would be an incomplete definition. His statement: 'they occurred' is a predicate for his statement 'the definition', and the alif in it is for absolute expression. His statement: 'and the rasm' means the complete one. And his statement: 'by the genus' means the proximate genus, as is taken from his statement: 'and the incomplete rasm...' etc. And his statement: 'and a property' means inclusive and necessary. Unlike what is not inclusive, like 'the knower' in relation to 'human', so it is not used to define because many individuals fall outside it. And unlike what is not necessary, like 'actually breathing' in relation to 'animal', so it is not used to define because individuals of the defined fall outside it at the time of separation. And it is required for the completeness of the rasm, in addition to what was mentioned, the precedence of the genus over the property; otherwise it would be an incomplete rasm – some verified scholars have stated this. His statement: 'together' means while they are both present.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage defines complete definition (hadd) and complete description (rasm) in the context of the five universals. The matn states that a complete hadd consists of a genus and a differentia, while a complete rasm consists of a genus and a property. The commentator (Bajuri) adds two conditions: First, the genus must precede the differentia/property, otherwise the definition/description becomes incomplete. Second, the property in a rasm must be both inclusive (shamilah) of all individuals and necessary (lazimah) – that is, inseparable from the essence. He gives examples: 'knower' is not inclusive of all humans (since some humans are not knowers at all times), so it cannot be used as a property for humans. 'Actually breathing' is not necessary for animals, as some animals are not breathing at a given moment (e.g., when asleep or drowned); thus it fails the necessity condition. The requirement of ordering (genus before differentia/property) ensures that the definition proceeds from the broader category to the more specific differentia. This mirrors the logical principle that a definition should capture the essence in a structured way.

Key Terms
الحَدّ
الجِنْس القَرِيب
الفَصْل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Bajuri, what condition is necessary for a complete hadd beyond having a genus and a differentia?
A) The differentia must be a single word
B) The genus must precede the differentia
C) The genus must be universal
D) The differentia must be inclusive

Key Takeaway
A complete hadd requires that the genus precede the differentia; otherwise it is incomplete.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Examine the definition: 'A human is a rational animal.' Identify the genus and differentia. Does the genus precede the differentia? Is this a complete hadd according to Bajuri's condition?
?

Hadd and Rasm
beginner
7 min
Conditions for a Complete Rasm (Description)
Bajuri explains property conditions for complete rasm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate whether a given description qualifies as a complete rasm by checking the property's inclusiveness and necessity, and the ordering of genus and property.

Core Idea
A complete rasm requires a genus followed by a property that is both inclusive and necessary.

In this segment, Bajuri expands on the conditions for a complete description (rasm al-tamm). Beyond having a genus and a property, the property must be shamilah (covering all individuals of the species) and lazimah (inseparable from the essence). He illustrates with examples: 'knower' fails inclusiveness; 'actually breathing' fails necessity. The genus must also precede the property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the phrase 'al-rasm al-tamm' (the complete description). The matn says 'al-rasm bi al-jins wa khassah ma'a'.
2
Define the property conditions
The property (khassa) must be 'shamilah lazimah' – all individuals of the species possess it at all times. 'Shamilah' means it covers every individual; 'lazimah' means it cannot be separated from the species.
These conditions prevent the description from being too narrow or too temporary.
3
Analyze the counterexamples
Bajuri gives two flawed properties: 'al-'alim' (the knower) for human – it is not inclusive because some humans are not knowers (e.g., infants). 'al-mutanafis bi al-fi'l' (actually breathing) for animal – it is not necessary because animals stop breathing at times (e.g., during hibernation).
4
Check the ordering condition
Like hadd, the genus must precede the property. Otherwise, the rasm is incomplete.
Bajuri attributes this condition to 'some verified scholars'.
5
Apply to a valid example
The property 'risible' (power to laugh) for human is often cited as a valid property. It is inclusive (all humans have the capacity) and necessary (inseparable from human nature). Genus 'animal' precedes it.

Source Text

قَوْلُهُ : (مَعَا) أَيْ : حَالَ كَوْنِهِمَا مَعاً .

Hadd and Rasm

Incomplete Hadd and Rasm: Types and Examples
Bajuri enumerates types of incomplete hadd and rasm, including subtypes and the third delayed-order case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each type of incomplete hadd and rasm and determine whether a given definition or description is complete or incomplete based on the presence and order of genus and differentia/property.

Core Idea
A complete definition requires the proximate genus followed by the differentia; any deviation makes it incomplete.

In the previous lesson, we learned the complete hadd and rasm. Now we examine what happens when the definition or description is incomplete. The matn and commentary distinguish between two main forms of incomplete hadd and rasm, each with a third subtle case involving the delay of the genus. Understanding these distinctions is essential for evaluating definitions in Islamic sciences like usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Look at the example 'Man is rational' or 'Man is a rational body'. The definiendum is 'man'. Determine what parts of the definition are present: genus, differentia, property?
2
Check for the proximate genus
Is the proximate genus 'animal' present? If not, the definition is incomplete. Note that a remote genus like 'body' does not suffice.
3
Examine the order of genus and differentia
If the genus is present but delayed after the differentia (e.g., 'rational animal'), the definition is still incomplete. The genus must precede the differentia.
4
Distinguish hadd from rasm
Hadd uses the differentia (essential), rasm uses the property (accidental). For each, the same pattern applies: missing proximate genus or delayed genus renders it incomplete.
5
Apply to Islamic science examples
Practice by evaluating a definition like 'Prayer is an act of worship consisting of specific sayings and actions'. Does it include the proximate genus? Is the order correct?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٤٢) وَنَاقِصُ الحَدِّ بِـ : فَصْلٍ أو مَعَ جِنْسٍ بَعيدٍ، لَا قَرِيبٍ وَقَعَا (٤٣) وَ(نَاقِصُ الرَّسْمِ) بِـ : خَاصَّةٍ فَقَطْ أَوْ مَعَ جِنْسِ أَبْعَدٍ قَدِ ارْتَبَط
الباجوري: قَوْلُهُ : (وَنَاقِصُ الحَدِّ) مِنْ إِضَافَةِ الصِّفَةِ لِلمَوْصُوفِ. وَقَوْلُهُ : (بِـ : فَصْلٍ ... إلخ) ذَكَرَ لِلحَدِّ النَّاقِصِ صُورَتَيْنِ :
(١) الأُولَى : أَنْ يَكُونَ بِالفَصْلِ وَحْدَهُ؛ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ : نَاطِقٌ».
(٢) الثَّانِيَةُ : أَنْ يَكُونَ بِالفَصْلِ مَعَ الجِنْسِ البَعِيدِ ؛ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ : جِسْمٌ نَاطِقٌ».
الأنبابي: قوله : (وَإِلَّا كَانَ حَدًّا نَاقِصاً) قال العطار : وأقول [۱۸/۴]: في ذلك نزاع ذكرناه في غير هذا المحل ب / ٢٦] ، وكذا يقال فيما يأتي. (۱) قوله : (گ: «العَالِمِ») أي: بالفعل. هو الصبان، انظر: «حاشية الصَّبَّان على الشَّرح الصَّغير للملوي (ص: ۳۱۳). (۲) انظر: حاشية العطار على السلم (لوحة : ٣٢).
وَبَقِيَتْ صُورَةٌ ثَالِثَةٌ، وَهِيَ :
(٣) - أَنْ يَأْتِيَ بِالجِنْسِ القَرِيبِ وَالفَصْلِ ، لَكِنْ مَعَ تَأْخِيرِ الجِنْسِ عَنِ الفَصْلِ - كَمَا يُعْلَمُ مِمَّا مَرَّ : - كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ : نَاطِقُ حَيَوَانُ».
وَمَا ذَكَرَهُ المُصَنِّفُ هُنَا مِنْ كَوْنِ الحَدِّ النَّاقِصِ يَكُونُ بِالفَصْلِ وَحْدَهُ مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَى جَوَازِ التَّعْرِيفِ بِالمُفْرَدِ، وَهُوَ مَذْهَبُ المُتَأخِّرِينَ مِنَ المَنَاطِقَةِ، وَكَذَا مَا ذَكَرَهُ بَعْدُ مِنْ كَوْنِ الرَّسْمِ النَّاقِصِ يَكُونُ بِالخَاصَّةِ وَحْدَهَا، كَمَا لَا يَخْفَى.
قَوْلُهُ : (أو مَعَا) مَعْطُوفٌ عَلَى مَحْذُوفٍ، وَالتَّقْدِيرُ: بِفَصْلٍ وَحْدَهُ، أَوْ مَعاً .
قَوْلُهُ : (لَا قَرِيبٍ) تَأْكِيدٌ لِمَا قَبْلَهُ .
قَوْلُهُ : (وَقَعَا) خَبَرٌ عَنْ قَوْلِهِ : وَنَاقِصُ الحَدِّ، وَالأَلِفُ لِلإِطْلَاقِ .
قَوْلُهُ : (وَنَاقِصُ الرَّسْمِ) مِنْ إِضَافَةِ الصِّفَةِ لِلمَوْصُوفِ، كَمَا مَرَّ فِي نَظِيرِهِ.
وَقَوْلُهُ : ( بـ : خَاصَّةٍ فَقَطْ) لَا بُدَّ أَنْ تَكُونَ تِلْكَ الخَاصَّةُ شَامِلَةً لَازِمَةً لِمَا تَقَدَّمَ، وَذَلِكَ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ : ضَاحِكٌ».
وقوله : (أَوْ مَعَ جِنْسِ أَبْعَدٍ) بِالتَّنْوِينِ لِلضَّرُورَةِ، وَالمُرَادُ بِهِ : البَعِيدُ ، وَذَلِكَ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ : جِسْمٌ ضَاحِكٌ».
فَهَاتَانِ صُورَتَانِ، وَبَقِيَتْ صُورَةٌ ثَالِثَةٌ وَهِيَ : أَنْ يَأْتِيَ بِالجِنْسِ القَرِيبِ وَالخَاصَّةِ، لَكِنْ مَعَ تَأخِيرِ الجِنْسِ عَنِ الخَاصَّةِ، كَمَا يُعْلَمُ مِمَّا تَقَدَّمَ؛ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ: ضَاحِكٌ حَيَوَانُ».
(1) الشرشيمي : قوله : (لَكِنْ مَعَ تَأخِيرِ الجِنْسِ عَنِ الفَصْلِ) قد يقال : أيُّ فائدة لذلك التَّأخير، بل يُقال : إنَّه كعدم ذكره أصلاً، ويمكن أنَّ التصريح بجزئي الماهية ، ولم يمتنع الإتيان بالعام هنا بخلافه فيما سبق في قوله : «الإنسان» في قوله : «الإنسان حَيَوَان نام أو حسَّاس، فإنَّه لا يصح بالمساوي، ولا بالأعم، مع أنَّ الأعم منه تصريح بجزئي الماهية أيضاً، والفرقُ بينهما : أنَّ ذكره الفصل هنا مغن عن ذكره غيره بعده، فذكر الجنس إن لم يفد لم يضر، بخلافه فيما سبق، فإنَّ ذكر الجنس القريب واقع موقعة، فيتعيَّن الإتيان بالأخص بعده ، ولا يعترض على ذكره هو .
(42) And the incomplete hadd is by a differentia, or together with a remote genus – not a proximate one – it occurred. (43) And the incomplete rasm is by a property only, or with a more remote genus it has been connected. Al-Bajuri: His statement: 'and the incomplete hadd' is an annexation of the adjective to the described. And his statement: 'by a differentia... etc.' He mentioned for the incomplete hadd two images: (1) The first: that it be by the differentia alone; as if one says: 'Man is rational.' (2) The second: that it be by the differentia together with the remote genus; as if one says: 'Man is a rational body.' Al-Anbabi: His statement: 'otherwise it would be an incomplete hadd' – al-Attar said: And I say [18/4]: there is a dispute regarding that which we mentioned elsewhere... (and so on, including footnotes). And a third image remains, which is: (3) That one brings the proximate genus and the differentia, but with delay of the genus after the differentia – as is known from what has passed – as if one says: 'Man is a rational animal.' And what the author mentioned here about the incomplete hadd being by the differentia alone is based on the permissibility of definition by a single term, and that is the doctrine of the later logicians. And likewise what he later mentioned about the incomplete rasm being by the property alone, as is clear. His statement: 'or together' is coordinated with an omitted element, the meaning: by a differentia alone, or together. His statement: 'not a proximate one' is emphasis of what preceded it. His statement: 'it occurred' is a predicate for his statement 'and the incomplete hadd', and the alif is for absolute expression. His statement: 'and the incomplete rasm' is an annexation of the adjective to the described, as passed in its counterpart. And his statement: 'by a property only' – that property must be inclusive and necessary as previously mentioned, and that is as if one says: 'Man is risible.' And his statement: 'or with a more remote genus' with nunation for poetic necessity, and what is meant is the remote one; and that is as if one says: 'Man is a risible body.' So these are two images, and a third image remains, which is: that one brings the proximate genus and the property, but with delay of the genus after the property, as is known from what has passed; as if one says: 'Man is a risible animal.' (1) Al-Shirshimi: His statement: 'but with delay of the genus after the differentia' – it may be said: What benefit is there in that delay? Rather, it is as if it were not mentioned at all. It is possible that the specification of the parts of the essence is intended, and it is not prohibited to bring the general here unlike what preceded in his statement: 'man is an animal that sleeps or feels', for that is not valid with the coextensive nor with the more general, even though the more general is a specification of the parts of the essence as well. And the difference between them is that mentioning the differentia here suffices for mentioning anything else after it, so mentioning the genus – if it does not benefit – does not harm. Unlike what preceded, for mentioning the proximate genus occurs in its proper place, so it is necessary to bring the more specific after it, and no objection is raised to mentioning it.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage discusses incomplete definitions (hadd naqis) and incomplete descriptions (rasm naqis). The matn states that an incomplete hadd is formed by either (1) the differentia alone, or (2) the differentia plus a remote genus, but not a proximate genus. Similarly, an incomplete rasm is formed by either (1) the property alone, or (2) the property plus a more remote genus. The commentator (Bajuri) then expands: The incomplete hadd has two images (later he adds a third). The first image is defining 'man' as 'rational' (just the differentia). The second is defining 'man' as 'rational body' (using the remote genus 'body' instead of 'animal'). A third image emerges from the condition of ordering: if one brings the proximate genus but delays it after the differentia, e.g., 'man is a rational animal', the definition is still incomplete because the genus should precede the differentia. The text notes that the permissibility of defining by a single term (like 'rational') is a doctrine of later logicians, implying there is disagreement. For the incomplete rasm, similar images exist: by property alone ('man is risible'), by property with a more remote genus ('man is a risible body'), and a third image with the proximate genus delayed ('man is a risible animal'). Finally, a marginal note by al-Shirshimi addresses a nuance: Why would delaying the genus matter? He argues that mentioning the differentia alone is sufficient to specify the essence, so adding a delayed genus is not harmful, unlike situations where the genus is mentioned first, which then necessitates a specific differentia. This highlights the logical subtlety that the order of terms in a definition reflects the logical priority of genus over differentia.

الحَدّ النَّاقِص
الرَّسْم النَّاقِص
الفَصْل
الخَاصَّة
الجِنْس البَعِيد
تَأخِير الجِنْس

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) الإنسان: جسم ناطق (Man is a rational body)
C) الإنسان: ناطق حيوان (Man is a rational animal)
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
A complete definition requires the proximate genus followed by the differentia; any deviation—missing genus, remote genus, or delayed genus—makes the definition incomplete, and similarly for descriptions using property.

Types of Incomplete Definition (Had Naqis)
Author enumerates forms of incomplete definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three forms of incomplete definition (had naqis) as described by al-Bajuri and apply them to Islamic legal definitions.

Core Idea
An incomplete definition is not faulty — it is simply missing a component or has an order issue.

In the previous lesson, we learned about complete definitions. Now, al-Bajuri explains that definitions can be incomplete yet still valid. Understanding these incomplete forms helps you recognise when a definition is merely imprecise rather than wrong.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three forms
From the passage, list the three ways to form an incomplete definition: (1) differentia alone, (2) differentia + distant genus, (3) proximate genus + differentia with delayed order.
2
Understand the differentia-alone form
Note that this is based on the view of later logicians who permit defining with a single term. Example: 'Man is rational.'
3
Apply to an Islamic concept
Think of a term like 'wajib' in fiqh. An incomplete definition could be 'Wajib is that which is rewarded if done' (property alone) – that is a rasm, not a hadd.
4
Distinguish complete vs incomplete
Explain that had naqis lacks either the proximate genus or the correct order; complete hadd has both genus (proximate) and differentia in order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وناقص الحَدٌ» بـ: فَصْلِ اوْمَعَا جِنْسٍ بَعيـ وَ(نَاقِصُ الرَّسْمِ بِـ: خَاصَةٍ فَقَدْ أَوْ مَعَ جِنسٍ بَعيدٍ، لَا قَرِيبٍ وَقَعَا. أَوْ مَعَ جِنْسِ أَبْعَدٍ قَدِ ارْتَبَط. الباجوري: وَبَقِيَتْ صُورَةٌ ثَالِثَةٌ، وَهِيَ: أَنْ يَأْتِيَ بِالجِنْسِ القَرِيبِ وَالفَصْلِ، لَكِنْ مَعَ تَأْخِيرِ الجِنْسِ عَنِ الفَصْلِ - كَمَا يُعْلَمُ مِمَّا مَرَّ: - كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ : نَاطِقُ حَيَوَانُ». وَمَا ذَكَرَهُ المُصَنِّفُ هُنَا مِنْ كَوْنِ الحَدِّ النَّاقِصِ يَكُونُ بِالفَصْلِ وَحْدَهُ مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَى جَوَازِ التَّعْرِيفِ بِالمُفْرَدِ، وَهُوَ مَذْهَبُ المُتَأخّرِينَ مِنَ المَنَاطِقَةِ، وَكَذَا مَا ذَكَرَهُ بَعْدُ مِنْ كَوْنِ الرَّسْمِ النَّاقِص يَكُونُ بِالخَاصَّةِ وَحْدَهَا، كَمَا لَا يَخْفَى. قَوْلُهُ : (اوْ مَعَا) مَعْطُوفٌ عَلَى مَحْذُوفٍ، وَالتَّقْدِيرُ: بِفَضْلٍ وَحْدَهُ، أَوْ مَعاً . قَوْلُهُ : (لَا قَرِيبٍ) تَأْكِيدٌ لِمَا قَبْلَهُ . قَوْلُهُ : (وَقَعَا) خَبَرٌ عَنْ قَوْلِهِ : وَنَاقِصُ الحَدٌ»، و«الأَلِفُ لِلإِطْلَاقِ . قَوْلُهُ : (وَانَاقِصُ الرَّسْمِ مِنْ إِضَافَةِ الصَّفَةِ لِلمَوْصُوفِ، كَمَا مَرَّ فِي نَظِيرِهِ. وَقَوْلُهُ : ( بـ: خَاصَةٍ فَقَط لَا بُدَّ أَنْ تَكُونَ تِلْكَ الخَاصَّةُ شَامِلَةٌ لَازِمَةٌ لِمَا تَقَدَّمَ، وَذَلِكَ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ : ضَاحِكَ». وقوله : (أَوْ مَعَ جِنْسِ أَبْعَدٍ) بِالتَّنْوِينِ لِلضَّرُورَةِ، وَالمُرَادُ بِهِ : البَعِيدُ ، وَذَلِكَ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ : جسْم ضَاحِكَ». فَهَاتَانِ صُورَتَانِ، وَبَقِيَتْ صُورَةٌ ثَالِثَةٌ وَهِيَ : أَنْ يَأْتِيَ بِالجِنْسِ القَرِيبِ وَالخَاصَّةِ، لَكِنْ مَعَ تَأخِيرِ الجِنْسِ عَنِ الخَاصَّةِ، كَمَا يُعْلَمُ مِمَّا تَقَدَّمَ؛ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ: ضَاحِكٌ حَيَوَانُ».
And the incomplete definition (is formed) with a differentia, or together with a distant genus. And the incomplete description (is formed) with a property only, or with a more distant genus, not a proximate one, it occurs. Or with a most distant genus it is connected. al-Bajuri: And a third form remains: to bring the proximate genus and the differentia, but with the genus delayed after the differentia – as known from what passed: like one says 'Man is a rational animal'. And what the author mentioned here that the incomplete definition occurs with the differentia alone is based on the permissibility of definition by a single term, and that is the school of the later logicians. And similarly what he mentioned later that the incomplete description occurs with the property alone, as is not hidden. His saying 'or together' is conjoined to an omitted element, the estimation: with a differentia alone, or together. His saying 'not proximate' is an emphasis of what preceded. His saying 'occurs' is a predicate for 'incomplete definition', and the alif is for absolute (mood). His saying 'and the incomplete description' is attribution of the adjective to the described, as passed in its counterpart. And his saying 'with a property only' – that property must be comprehensive and necessary for what preceded, like one says 'Man is laughing'. And his saying 'or with a most distant genus' – with nunation due to necessity, and what is meant by it is the distant, like one says 'Man is a laughing body'. So these are two forms, and a third form remains: to bring the proximate genus and the property, but with the genus delayed after the property, as known from what passed; like one says 'Man is a laughing animal'.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage defines two types of incomplete definitions: incomplete definition (had naqis) and incomplete description (rasm naqis). The matn states that incomplete definition is formed either with a differentia alone or with a differentia plus a distant genus (not a proximate one). Incomplete description is formed with a property alone or with a property plus a more distant genus. The commentator then adds a third form for had naqis: combining a proximate genus with a differentia but delaying the genus after the differentia, e.g., 'Man is a rational animal'. He notes that the author's claim that had naqis can be just the differentia relies on the permissibility of defining with a single term, a view of later logicians. The commentary then breaks down each Arabic phrase: 'or together' completes an omitted phrase; 'not proximate' emphasizes; 'occurs' is the predicate; 'and the incomplete description' relates to previous similar constructions. For rasm naqis, the property must be comprehensive and necessary (lazim). Examples: 'Man is laughing' (property alone) and 'Man is a laughing body' (property with more distant genus). Finally, a third form for rasm naqis: proximate genus with property but with genus delayed, e.g., 'Man is a laughing animal'.

Key Terms

فصل
جنس بعيد
جنس قريب

B) Differentia with proximate genus
C) Differentia with distant genus
D) Proximate genus with differentia but delayed order

Key Takeaway
An incomplete definition can be formed in three ways, and its validity depends on the context, especially the permissibility of single-term definitions.

Types of Incomplete Description (Rasm Naqis)
Author explains forms of incomplete description.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three forms of incomplete description (rasm naqis) and construct examples using Islamic concepts.

Core Idea
A description (rasm) is always incomplete by nature, but some forms are more complete than others.

While definitions aim for essence, descriptions rely on properties. Al-Bajuri now explains how incomplete descriptions are formed, including a third form similar to the incomplete definition.

Guided Path
1
List the forms of rasm naqis
From the passage: (1) property alone, (2) property with a more distant genus, (3) proximate genus with property but with genus delayed.
2
Note the conditions
The property must be comprehensive (shamil) and necessary (lazim). Example: 'laughing' for man.
3
Apply to an Islamic concept
Define 'iman' (faith) as 'affirmation with the heart' (property alone) – that's a rasm naqis.
4
Contrast with had naqis
Rasm naqis uses a property (khassa) while had naqis uses a differentia (fasl). The structure is parallel.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وناقص الحَدٌ» بـ: فَصْلِ اوْمَعَا جِنْسٍ بَعيـ وَ(نَاقِصُ الرَّسْمِ بِـ: خَاصَةٍ فَقَدْ أَوْ مَعَ جِنسٍ بَعيدٍ، لَا قَرِيبٍ وَقَعَا. أَوْ مَعَ جِنْسِ أَبْعَدٍ قَدِ ارْتَبَط. الباجوري: وَبَقِيَتْ صُورَةٌ ثَالِثَةٌ، وَهِيَ: أَنْ يَأْتِيَ بِالجِنْسِ القَرِيبِ وَالفَصْلِ، لَكِنْ مَعَ تَأْخِيرِ الجِنْسِ عَنِ الفَصْلِ - كَمَا يُعْلَمُ مِمَّا مَرَّ: - كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ : نَاطِقُ حَيَوَانُ». وَمَا ذَكَرَهُ المُصَنِّفُ هُنَا مِنْ كَوْنِ الحَدِّ النَّاقِصِ يَكُونُ بِالفَصْلِ وَحْدَهُ مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَى جَوَازِ التَّعْرِيفِ بِالمُفْرَدِ، وَهُوَ مَذْهَبُ المُتَأخّرِينَ مِنَ المَنَاطِقَةِ، وَكَذَا مَا ذَكَرَهُ بَعْدُ مِنْ كَوْنِ الرَّسْمِ النَّاقِص يَكُونُ بِالخَاصَّةِ وَحْدَهَا، كَمَا لَا يَخْفَى. قَوْلُهُ : (اوْ مَعَا) مَعْطُوفٌ عَلَى مَحْذُوفٍ، وَالتَّقْدِيرُ: بِفَضْلٍ وَحْدَهُ، أَوْ مَعاً . قَوْلُهُ : (لَا قَرِيبٍ) تَأْكِيدٌ لِمَا قَبْلَهُ . قَوْلُهُ : (وَقَعَا) خَبَرٌ عَنْ قَوْلِهِ : وَنَاقِصُ الحَدٌ»، و«الأَلِفُ لِلإِطْلَاقِ . قَوْلُهُ : (وَانَاقِصُ الرَّسْمِ مِنْ إِضَافَةِ الصَّفَةِ لِلمَوْصُوفِ، كَمَا مَرَّ فِي نَظِيرِهِ. وَقَوْلُهُ : ( بـ: خَاصَةٍ فَقَط لَا بُدَّ أَنْ تَكُونَ تِلْكَ الخَاصَّةُ شَامِلَةٌ لَازِمَةٌ لِمَا تَقَدَّمَ، وَذَلِكَ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ : ضَاحِكَ». وقوله : (أَوْ مَعَ جِنْسِ أَبْعَدٍ) بِالتَّنْوِينِ لِلضَّرُورَةِ، وَالمُرَادُ بِهِ : البَعِيدُ ، وَذَلِكَ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ : جسْم ضَاحِكَ». فَهَاتَانِ صُورَتَانِ، وَبَقِيَتْ صُورَةٌ ثَالِثَةٌ وَهِيَ : أَنْ يَأْتِيَ بِالجِنْسِ القَرِيبِ وَالخَاصَّةِ، لَكِنْ مَعَ تَأخِيرِ الجِنْسِ عَنِ الخَاصَّةِ، كَمَا يُعْلَمُ مِمَّا تَقَدَّمَ؛ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ: ضَاحِكٌ حَيَوَانُ».

Evaluating Composite Definitions with Accident and Property
Commentator lists and evaluates additional definition forms involving 'arad 'amm, khassa, and fasl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify composite definitions as hadd or rasm and rank them according to al-Bajuri's criteria.

Core Idea
Adding a general accident strengthens a definition; rejecting these composites is weak.

You have learned about hadd and rasm. However, there are hybrid forms that combine accidental and essential terms. In this passage, al-Bajuri clarifies the status of definitions that pair a general accident with a property or differentia, and the differentia with a property. He also addresses whether a general accident alone can serve as a definition. This lesson will help you navigate these nuanced evaluations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three composite forms
Locate in the Arabic the three combinations: (1) general accident with property, (2) general accident with differentia, (3) differentia with property. Note the examples given: 'walking, laughing' (general accident+property), 'walking, rational' (general accident+differentia), 'rational, laughing' (differentia+property).
These are all for the species 'man'.
2
Classify each composite as hadd or rasm
According to al-Bajuri citing al-Sayyid: the combination of general accident+property yields an incomplete description (rasm naqis). The other two (general accident+differentia and differentia+property) yield an incomplete definition (hadd naqis). Understand that a rasm uses accidental features, while a hadd uses essential ones.
A hadd naqis is still a definition, but lacks some precision; a rasm naqis is a description.
3
Determine the strength ranking
Al-Bajuri states that the first composite (general accident+property) is stronger than using the property alone. The second and third composites are more complete than using the differentia alone. He rejects the view that none of these are valid.
Strength here means informativeness and clarity.
4
Understand why adding a general accident strengthens
Al-Bajuri argues that adding a general accident to a property or differentia does not weaken the definition; it strengthens it. This counters the claim that such composites are invalid. Reflect on the logical benefit: the general accident provides additional distinguishing information.
This is a key point against the opposition narrated by al-Hafid.
5
Resolve the issue of general accident alone
The passage notes that a general accident alone does not serve as a definition. Al-Bajuri favors the view that this is because definition cannot be by something more general (al-a'am). Consider why that is: a general accident applies beyond the species, so it fails to specify.
Some scholars hesitated on the reason, but al-Bajuri leans towards the impermissibility of definition by the more general.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباجوري تنبيه : بقي التعريف بالعرض العام مع الخاصة، أو مع الفصل؛ كأن يقال: «الإنسان : ماش ضاحك، أو : ناطق». وكذا التعريف بالفصل مع الخاصة؛ كأن يقال: «الإنسان: ناطق ضاحك». والصواب - كما قال السيد : - أن الأول رسم ناقص وهو أقوى من الخاصة وحدها، وأن كلًا من الثاني والثالث حد ناقص وهو أكمل من الفصل وحده. وأما ما نقله الحفيد عن بعضهم من عدم اعتبار كل من هذه الثلاثة فلا يخفى ضعفه، بل رده؛ لأن انضمام العرض العام إلى الخاصة أو إلى الفصل إن لم يفد لم يضعف، والواقع أنه مقو كما ذكره السيد، وكذا انضمام الخاصة إلى الفصل. وظاهر كلامهم : أن العرض العام وحده لا يقع معرِّفاً، وهل هو مبني على عدم جواز التعريف بالأعم، أو لا؟ توقف فيه بعضهم، والأقرب الأول، فليحرر.
al-Bajuri: A note: There remains definition with the general accident along with a property, or with a differentia; like one says 'Man is a walking, laughing [thing]', or 'a rational [thing]'. And likewise definition with the differentia along with a property; like one says 'Man is a rational, laughing [thing]'. And the correct view – as al-Sayyid said – is that the first is an incomplete description which is stronger than the property alone, and that each of the second and third is an incomplete definition which is more complete than the differentia alone. As for what al-Hafid transmitted from some of them of not considering any of these three, its weakness is not hidden; rather it is rejected, because the addition of the general accident to the property or to the differentia, if it does not benefit, does not weaken, and the reality is that it strengthens as al-Sayyid mentioned. And likewise the addition of the property to the differentia. And the apparent meaning of their statements is that the general accident alone does not serve as a definition. And is this based on the impermissibility of definition by the more general, or not? Some suspended judgment on it, and the closest is the first, so it should be investigated.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a note (tanbih) by al-Bajuri listing additional forms of definition not covered earlier. He mentions three: (1) definition with a general accident ('arad 'amm) combined with a property (khassa); (2) definition with a general accident combined with a differentia (fasl); (3) definition with a differentia combined with a property. Examples: 'Man is a walking, laughing [thing]' (general accident + property), 'Man is a rational, laughing [thing]' (differentia + property). Al-Bajuri then gives the correct ruling as per al-Sayyid: the first combination (general accident + property) yields an incomplete description, but stronger than using property alone. The second and third (general accident + differentia, and differentia + property) yield an incomplete definition, more complete than using differentia alone. He refutes the opinion of some (narrated by al-Hafid) that these three forms are not valid at all, arguing that adding a general accident does not weaken; rather it strengthens. He also notes that a general accident alone is not a valid definition, and this is likely based on the rule that definition cannot be with a more general term, though some hesitated.

خاصة
فصل

Key Takeaway
Composite definitions using a general accident with a property or differentia are valid and often stronger than using a single term, contrary to some rejections.

Verbal Definition: Synonym Replacement
Author defines verbal definition as replacing a word with a more famous synonym.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi) and distinguish it from a real definition (hadd/rasm).

Core Idea
A verbal definition merely swaps words; it does not reveal the essence.

Definitions in logic are of two kinds: real (hadd/rasm) and verbal (lafzi). This passage introduces the verbal definition, which simply replaces an unfamiliar term with a more famous synonym. It does not provide new conceptual content but merely clarifies the referent of a word. The commentator al-Bajuri refines the matn's wording to avoid a common confusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the term being defined in the passage. The matn defines 'verbal definition' (mu'arraf lafzi).
2
Extract the defining condition
The definition given is 'replacement of a word with a more famous synonym'. Note that the matn says the definition is the 'replacement', but the commentator corrects this: the definition is the substitute word itself, not the act.
This shows sensitivity to the object of definition: definitions are words, not actions.
3
Examine the synonym example
The example is defining 'al-burr' as 'al-qamh'. Both are Arabic synonyms for wheat. This is a pure verbal definition — no genus or differentia are given.
Contrast with a real definition like 'al-insan hayawan natiq' which reveals the essence.
4
Distinguish from real definition
A real definition (hadd) gives the genus and differentia, thus explaining what the thing is. A verbal definition only links words to known synonyms. If someone already knows 'qamh', they now know 'burr' refers to the same thing, but not its essence.
This distinction is crucial for using definitions in Islamic sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في المعرفات (٤٤) وَمَا بِـ «لَفْظِيّ» لَدَيْهِمْ شُهِرَا تَبْدِيلُ لَفْظُ بِرَدِيفٍ أَشْـهَــرَا الباجوري قَوْلُهُ : (وَمَا بِـ «لَفْظِيّ»... إلخ) أَيْ : وَالَّذِي شُهِرَ عِنْدَهُمْ بِـ المُعَرِّفِ اللَّفْظِيِّ... إلخ»، «مَا اسْمٌ مَوْصُولٌ ، وَشُهِرَ) صِلَتُهَا، وَلَدَيْهِمْ بِمَعْنَى : عِنْدَهُمْ ، ظَرْفٌ لِتِلْكَ الصَّلَةِ . وَقَوْلُهُ : (تَبْدِيلُ ... إلخ) فِيهِ تَسَامُح ؛ لِأَنَّ المُعَرِّفَ اللَّفْظِيَّ لَيْسَ نَفْسَ التَّبْدِيلِ، بَلِ اللَّفْظُ الَّذِي أَتَى بِهِ بَدَلاً ؛ إِذِ التَّعَارِيفُ مِنْ قَبِيلِ الأَلْفَاظِ (٣) ، وَذَلِكَ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ فِي تَعْرِيفِ «البُرِّ»: «هُوَ : القَمْحُ».
Section on Definitions. (44) And what is known among them as 'verbal (definition)' is the replacement of a word with a more famous synonym. al-Bajuri: His saying: 'And what is known...' etc. – meaning: that which is famous among them as the verbal definition... etc., 'ma' is a relative noun, 'shuhira' is its relative clause, and 'ladayhim' means 'with them', an adverb for that clause. And his saying: 'replacement...' etc. - there is looseness in it, because the verbal definition is not itself the replacement, but rather the word that is brought as a substitute; since definitions are of the category of words. And that is like one says in defining 'al-burr': 'It is: al-qamh'.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage introduces the verbal definition (ta'rif lafzi) as a new section. The matn states that what is known among the logicians as 'verbal definition' is the replacement of a word with a more famous synonym. The commentator explains that the matn's phrasing is loose: the verbal definition is not the act of replacement itself but the substitute word. He gives an example: defining 'burr' (wheat) as 'qamh' (a synonym). The point is that verbal definitions simply replace an unfamiliar term with a better-known one without adding conceptual content.

Composite Definitions: Common Property, Special Property, and Differentia
Al-Bajuri examines three composite definitions and refutes a contrary opinion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a given composite definition as either a deficient rasm, deficient hadd, or complete definition, and justify your classification based on the components used.

Core Idea
Combining multiple properties strengthens a definition, even if it remains deficient.

In this passage, al-Bajuri clarifies the status of definitions that pair a common property with a special property or differentia, and those that pair differentia with special property. He refutes the claim that such combinations are invalid, arguing instead that they produce stronger definitions. Understanding this hierarchy is crucial for evaluating the precision of definitions in Islamic sciences, such as when defining legal terms in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three composite definitions listed by al-Bajuri
Al-Bajuri lists three types: (1) common property + special property, (2) common property + differentia, (3) differentia + special property. For example, defining 'human' as 'walking, laughing' (common + special), 'walking, rational' (common + differentia), or 'rational, laughing' (differentia + special).
2
Classify each type according to al-Bajuri's ruling
The first type (common + special) is a deficient descriptive definition (rasm naqis). The second and third types (involving the differentia) are deficient real definitions (hadd naqis). Each is stronger than using the respective property alone.
3
Understand why combining properties strengthens the definition
Al-Bajuri argues that adding a common property to a special property or differentia does not weaken the definition; rather, it strengthens it by providing additional distinguishing characteristics, even if the definition remains deficient due to the absence of genus.
4
Apply al-Anbabi's refinement regarding genus type
Al-Anbabi notes that if the definition also includes the proximate genus (al-jins al-qarib) along with the differentia and special property or common property, it becomes a complete real definition (hadd tamm). If the remote genus is used, it remains a deficient real definition (hadd naqis).
This is a further elaboration from the commentary of al-Sabban.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباجوري تنبيه :
- بَقِيَ التَّعْرِيفُ بِالعَرَضِ العَام مَعَ الخَاصَّةِ ، أَوْ مَعَ الفَصْلِ ؛ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الإِنْسَانُ : مَاشٍ ضَاحِكٌ، أو : نَاطِقُ».
- وَكَذَا التَّعْرِيفُ بِالفَصْلِ مَعَ الخَاصَّةِ ؛ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ: «الْإِنْسَانُ: نَاطِقٌ ضَاحِكَ». وَالصَّوَابُ - كَمَا قَالَهُ السَّيِّدُ :- : أَنَّ الأَوَّلَ رَسُمٌ نَاقِصٌ وَهُوَ أَقْوَى مِنَ الخَاصَّةِ وَحْدَهَا ، وَأَنَّ كُلًّا مِنَ الثَّانِي وَالثَّالِثِ حَدٌ نَاقِصٌ وَهُوَ أَكْمَلُ مِنَ الفَصْلِ وَحْدَهُ .
وَأَمَّا مَا نَقَلَهُ الحَفِيدُ عَنْ بَعْضِهِمْ مِنْ عَدَمِ اعْتِبَارِ كُلِّ مِنْ هَذِهِ الثَّلَاثَةِ فَلَا يَخْفَى ضَعْفُهُ، بَلْ رَدُّهُ ؛ لأَنَّ انْضِمَامَ العَرَضِ العَامُ إِلَى الخَاصَّةِ أَوْ إِلَى الفَصْلِ إِنْ لَمْ يَفْوَ لَمْ يَضْعُفُ، وَالوَاقِعُ أَنَّهُ مُقَوِّ كَمَا ذَكَرَهُ السَّيِّدُ (۲) ، وَكَذَا انْضِمَامُ الخَاصَّةِ إِلَى الفَصْلِ.
وَظَاهِرُ كَلَامِهِمْ : أَنَّ العَرَضَ العَامَ وَحْدَهُ لَا يَقَعُ مُعَرِّفاً، وَهَلْ هُوَ مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَى عَدَمِ جَوَازِ التَّعْرِيفِ بالأعم، أَوْ لا؟ تَوَقَّفَ فِيهِ بَعْضُهُمْ، وَالأَقْرَبُ الأَوَّلُ، فَلْيُحَرَّرُ.
الأنبابي :
قوله : (بَقِيَ التَّعْرِيفُ بِالعَرَضِ العَام ... إلخ) بقي أيضاً : التَّعريف بالجنس بنوعيه مع الفصل، والخاصة، أو العَرَض العام .
والظَّاهِرُ أنَّ الجنس القريب مع الفصل والخاصَّة أوِ العَرَض العام حد تام، وأنَّ الجنس البعيد مع الفصل والخاصَّة أوِ العَرَض العام حد ناقص . اهـ (صبان (٤) .
Al-Bajuri's notice: Remains the definition by the common property with the special property, or with the differentia; such as saying: 'Man: walking, laughing', or: 'rational'. And likewise the definition by the differentia with the special property; such as saying: 'Man: rational, laughing'. And the correct view - as al-Sayyid said - is that the first is a deficient descriptive definition (rasm) and it is stronger than the special property alone, and that each of the second and third is a deficient real definition (hadd) and it is more complete than the differentia alone. As for what al-Hafidh transmitted from some of them of not considering each of these three, its weakness is not hidden; rather it is rejected; because the joining of the common property to the special property or to the differentia, if it does not miss, it does not weaken; and the reality is that it strengthens, as al-Sayyid mentioned, and likewise the joining of the special property to the differentia. And the apparent meaning of their words is that the common property alone does not occur as a definer. And is it based on the impermissibility of definition by the more common, or not? Some of them were undecided about it, and the closer is the first, so let it be written. Al-Anbabi: His words: 'Remains the definition by the common property... etc.' Remains also: the definition by the genus with its two types with the differentia, and the special property, or the common property. And the apparent meaning is that the proximate genus with the differentia and the special property or the common property is a complete real definition, and that the remote genus with the differentia and the special property or the common property is a deficient real definition. End. (al-Sabban, 4).
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a clarification of types of definitions that combine multiple characteristics. The author, al-Bajuri, begins by listing three specific composite definitions: (1) common property (like 'walking') plus special property (like 'laughing'), (2) common property plus differentia (like 'rational'), and (3) differentia plus special property. For example, defining 'human' as 'walking, laughing' falls into the first type. The correct position, attributed to al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani, is that the first type is a deficient descriptive definition (rasm naqis) but stronger than using the special property alone. The second and third types are deficient real definitions (hadd naqis) but more complete than using the differentia alone. Al-Bajuri then refutes an opinion transmitted by al-Hafidh that none of these three are valid definitions, arguing that combining these properties strengthens rather than weakens the definition. He notes that the common property alone is never used as a definer, and the reasoning for that is likely the general principle that definition by a broader term is impermissible. Finally, al-Anbabi adds that definitions combining the proximate genus with the differentia and special property or common property yield a complete real definition, while using the remote genus yields only a deficient real definition. This highlights a hierarchy of definitional strength in Islamic logic.

Key Terms
العرض العام (al-'arad al-'amm) - common property
الخاصة (al-khassa) - special property
الفصل (al-fasl) - differentia
الرسم الناقص (al-rasm al-naqis) - deficient descriptive definition
الحد الناقص (al-hadd al-naqis) - deficient real definition

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Deficient descriptive definition (rasm naqis)

Key Takeaway
Composite definitions are valid and often stronger than single-property definitions, provided they combine appropriate logical components.

What is a Verbal Definition?
Al-Bajuri defines verbal definition and gives an example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define a verbal definition and identify its key feature: replacing a word with a more famous synonym.

Core Idea
A verbal definition replaces an obscure word with a more famous synonym.

In this lesson, we examine the verbal definition (al-ta'rif al-lafzi). Unlike a real definition (hadd), it does not break down the essence but simply substitutes a word for a more widely known equivalent. Al-Bajuri clarifies that the definition is the substitute word itself, not the act of replacement, and provides an example from the Arabic language.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and definiens
Find the word being defined (the obscure term) and the word used to define it (the more famous synonym). In the example, 'al-burr' is defined as 'al-qamh'.
2
Check the fame condition
The synonym must be more famous (ashhar) than the original word. If it is equally or less famous, the definition fails.
The author specifies 'more famous to the hearer'.
3
Distinguish between the act and the word
Al-Bajuri notes that the verbal definer is not the action of replacing but the word that replaces. This is a subtle point: definitions are words, not actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٤٤) وَمَا بِـ «لَفْظِيّ» لَدَيْهِمْ شُهِرَا تَبْدِيلُ لَفْظُ بِرَدِيفٍ أَشْـهَــرَا
الباجوري قوله: (وما بـ «لفظي»... إلخ) أَيْ : وَالَّذِي شُهِرَ عِنْدَهُمْ بِـ المُعَرِّفِ اللَّفْظِيّ... إلخ»، «مَا اسْمٌ مَوْصُولٌ ، وَشُهِرَ) صِلَتُهَا، وَلَدَيْهِمْ بِمَعْنَى : عِنْدَهُمْ ، ظَرْفٌ لِتِلْكَ الصَّلَةِ . وَقَوْلُهُ : (تَبْدِيلُ ... إلخ) فِيهِ تَسَامُح ; لِأَنَّ المُعَرِّفَ اللَّفْظِيَّ لَيْسَ نَفْسَ التَّبْدِيلِ، بَلِ اللَّفْظُ الَّذِي أَتَى بِهِ بَدَلاً ; إِذِ التَّعَارِيفُ مِنْ قَبِيلِ الأَلْفَاظِ (۳) ، وَذَلِكَ كَأَنْ يُقَالَ فِي تَعْرِيفِ «البُرِّ»: «هُوَ : القَمْحُ».
(٤٥) وَشَرْطُ كُلِّ: أَنْ يُرَى مُطَرِدَا» «مُنْعَكِساً»، و«ظَاهِراً» لَا أَبْعَدَا
وَقَوْلُهُ : (بِرَدِيفٍ) أَيْ : بِمُرَادِفٍ، فَهُوَ فَعِيلٌ ; بِمَعْنَى : مُفَاعِلٍ . وَقَوْلُهُ: (أَشْهَرًا) أَيْ: عِنْدَ السَّامِعِ ، وَاحْتَرَزَ بِذَلِكَ عَنِ : الرَّدِيفِ الأَخْفَى، أَوِ المُسَاوِي، كَمَا هُوَ ظَاهِرٌ. قَوْلُهُ : (وَشَرْطُ كُلِّ ... إلخ) ظَاهِرُ كَلَامِهِ : اعْتِبَارُ مَا ذَكَرَهُ مِنَ الشُّرُوطِ فِي اللَّفْظِيّ كَغَيْرِهِ. وَتَعَقَّبَهُ بَعْضُهُمْ : بِأَنَّهُ لَا مَعْنَى لِاشْتِرَاطِ هَذِهِ الأُمُورِ فِيهِ; لأَنَّهُ لَا يُعْقَلُ تَخَلَّفُ شَيْءٍ مِنْهَا عَنْهُ; إِذْ لَا يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يَكُونَ لَفْظُ الرَّدِيفِ الأَشْهَرِ غَيْرَ جَامِعِ وَلَا غَيْرَ مَانِعِ ; لِأَنَّ مَدْلُولَهُ عَيْنُ مَدْلُولِ اللَّفْظِ غَيْرِ الأَشْهَرِ، وَلَا يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يَكُونَ دُونَ المُعَرَّفِ وَلَا مُسَاوِياً ; لِأَنَّ الفَرَضَ أَنَّهُ أَشْهَرُ مِنْهُ، وَلَا مَجَازاً ; لأَنَّ المَجَازَ وَالحَقِيقَةَ لَيْسَا مُتَرَادِفَيْنِ، وَلَا يُمْكِنُ أَيْضاً دُخُولُ الدَّورِ فِيهِ، كَمَا صَرَّحَ بِهِ ابْنُ قَاسِمِ فِي الآيَاتِ، وَهَكَذَا البَاقِي. اهـ وَهُوَ وَجِيه. لَكِنْ نَاقَشَ بَعْضُ المُحَقِّقِينَ فِي قَوْلِهِ : وَهَكَذَا البَاقِي» بـ : أَنَّهُ يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يَكُونَ اللَّفْظُ الأَشْهَرُ مُشْتَرَكاً بَيْنَ مَعْنَى رَدِيفِهِ غَيْرِ الأَشْهَرِ وَبَيْنَ مَعْنى آخَرَ (۱) ، وَبِهَذَا يُعْلَمُ مَا فِي قَوْلِهِ : «لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُعْقَلُ تَخَلُّفُ شَيْءٍ مِنْهَا عَنْهُ، فَلْيُتَأَمَّلْ.
الأنبابي :
قوله : (لَكِنْ نَاقَشَ بَعْضُ المُحَقِّقِينَ ... إلخ) فيه نظر؛ لأنَّه إذا لم يكن الآخر مشتركاً لم يكن رديفاً، وعلى تسليم أنَّه رديف إذا كان المشترك خالياً مِنَ القرينة كان غير ظاهر، وهو خلاف الفرض، وإن كان كلٌّ منهما مشتركاً بين معنيين؛ إلَّا أنَّ أحدهما أشهر فيهما ، والآخر خفيًا فيهما ، لم يمتنع التعريف بالمشترك؛ لأنَّ محلَّ منعه إذا لم يرد به جميع معانيه، وهنا قد أريد به معنياه معاً، وإن كان أحدهما أشهر في معنى من معنيه، والآخر خفيًا فيهما ، كانتِ الشُّهرة في هذا المعنى قرينة على إرادة تعريف الآخر بالنسبة لأحد معنييه، وإن كان كل منهما مشتهراً في معنى غير ما اشتهر فيه الآخر، لم يصح التّعريف; لعدم الشُّهرة مِنَ الجهة التي قصد بها التعريف، فتأمل.
(1) الشرشيمي : قوله : (وَبَيْنَ مَعْنى آخَرَ ) أي : كما إذا وضع لفظ «القمح» مثلاً على ابن زيد» مثلاً، ونظر فيه بعضهم: بأنَّه لا ترادف; إذ المتبادر منه التّساوي من كل الوجوه وقوله فيما سبق : (وَلَا يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يَكُونَ دُونَ المُعَرَّفِ) أي : دونه الظهور، وهو المعبّر عنه في المتن بقوله: «لَا أَبْعَدًا».
(44) And that which is known among them as 'verbal' is the replacement of a word by a more famous synonym. Al-Bajuri: His words: 'And that which... etc.' Meaning: that which is well-known among them as the verbal definer... etc. 'Ma' is a relative noun, 'shuhira' is its relative clause, and 'ladayhim' means 'among them', an adverb for that clause. His words: 'replacement... etc.' contains looseness, because the verbal definer is not the replacement itself, but the word that is brought as a substitute, since definitions are of the type of words. And that is like when it is said in defining 'al-burr': 'It is: al-qamh'. (45) And the condition of every (definition) is that it be seen as universal, converse, and clear, not remote. And his words: 'by a synonym' i.e., by a synonymous word, so it is fa'il in the sense of mufa'il. And his words: 'more famous' i.e., to the hearer, and by that he excludes the less famous or equal synonym, as is apparent. His words: 'and the condition of every... etc.' The apparent meaning of his speech is the consideration of what he mentioned of the conditions in the verbal (definition) as in other (definitions). And some objected to him: that there is no meaning to stipulating these matters in it, because it is inconceivable that any of them be absent from it; since it is impossible for the word of the more famous synonym to be non-universal or non-exclusive, because its meaning is identical to the meaning of the less famous word; and it is impossible for it to be less than the definiendum or equal, because the assumption is that it is more famous than it; and it is impossible for it to be metaphorical, because the metaphorical and the literal are not synonyms; and it is also impossible for circularity to enter into it, as Ibn Qasim stated in (his commentary on) al-Ayat, and likewise the rest. End. And it is sound. However, some of the verifiers criticized him regarding his statement 'and likewise the rest', saying that it is possible for the more famous word to be polysemous between the meaning of its less famous synonym and another meaning. And by this it is known what is in his statement 'because it is inconceivable that any of them be absent from it', so let it be considered. Al-Anbabi: His words: 'However, some verifiers criticized... etc.' There is a consideration in it; because if the other is not polysemous, it is not a synonym. And granting that it is a synonym, if the polysemous word is free from a contextual indicator, it is not clear, contrary to the assumption. And if each of them is polysemous between two meanings, except that one of them is more famous in both, and the other is obscure in both, definition by the polysemous is not prevented, because the place of its prevention is when not all its meanings are intended; and here both meanings are intended together. And if one of them is more famous in one of its two meanings and the other is obscure in both, the fame in that meaning is an indicator of the intention to define the other with respect to one of its two meanings. And if each of them is famous in a meaning different from what the other is famous for, the definition is not valid, due to lack of fame from the aspect intended by the definition. So reflect. (1) Al-Shirshimi: His words: 'and another meaning' i.e., as if the word 'al-qamh' were placed on 'Zayd's son' for example. And some considered it, saying that there is no synonymy, since the immediate understanding is equality from all aspects; and his statement earlier 'and it is impossible for it to be less than the definiendum' means 'less in clarity', which is expressed in the text by 'not remote'.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage defines the verbal definition (al-ta'rif al-lafzi) and discusses its conditions. The matn first states that a verbal definition is replacing a word with a more famous synonym. Al-Bajuri explains that the definer is not the act of replacement but the substitute word itself, as definitions are linguistic. He gives an example: defining 'al-burr' (wheat) as 'al-qamh' (another word for wheat). The matn then lists conditions for all definitions: being universal (mutarid), converse (mun'akis), clear (zahir), and not remote (la ab'ad). Al-Bajuri notes that some scholars objected that these conditions are automatically satisfied for verbal definitions because the synonym has the exact same meaning, so it cannot lack universality or exclusivity, cannot be less famous or equal, cannot be metaphorical, and cannot involve circularity. However, a verifier raised a nuanced objection: the more famous synonym might be polysemous (mushtarak), having another meaning besides the intended one. In that case, the definition would be ambiguous and not clear. Al-Anbabi then provides a detailed analysis of various scenarios of polysemy and fame. He argues that if the polysemous word has no contextual indicator, it lacks clarity. If both words are polysemous and one is more famous in both meanings, defining by it is permissible if both meanings are intended. If one is more famous in one meaning only, that fame can serve as a contextual indicator. But if each is famous in a different meaning, the definition fails due to lack of relevant fame. This refined analysis shows that the conditions are not automatically satisfied in verbal definitions and require careful consideration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, what is a verbal definition?
A) Identifying the genus and differentia
B) Replacing a word with a more famous synonym
C) Defining a word by giving its opposite
D) Stating the definition in a more obscure way

Key Takeaway
A verbal definition is a linguistic substitution using a more famous synonym.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a verbal definition from your own knowledge: take a technical Islamic term (e.g., 'salat' is 'du'a' in a broader sense) and provide a more famous synonym. Check whether the synonym is indeed more famous.
?
Find a counterexample where a synonym used in a definition is not more famous; explain why it fails as a verbal definition.
